Complete Plan of the National Education Conference (III)

C. How to prepare the necessary school buildings and equipment in classrooms, those who should receive supplementary education number 202,435,277 people, according to item B.

Adding the number of out-of-school youths, then primary school buildings and classrooms are already full day and night and cannot accommodate any more. Assuming each classroom holds fifty people, with two shifts taking turns to use it, that is, one classroom is needed for every one hundred people. The number of classrooms is exactly equal to the number of teachers, 112,470. Generally, a single-level public supplementary school should use two rooms with adequate air and light, suitable in height and size, one large room as a classroom and one small room as an office.

This is absolutely essential. Moreover, the Ministry of Education has promulgated the regulations for promoting industry (Note 3). The former University Council also issued a general order to all provinces and cities to use established institutions and organizations to establish public education (Note 4). In the future, the school buildings for adult supplementary education will inevitably become the center of social reform. Therefore, the school building is naturally also a problem.

D. How to raise the required funds. According to the survey, it costs at least one dollar and forty cents to train each graduate of a public school (Note 5).

Accordingly, the adult supplementary education funds required for more than 202 million people is 283.4 million yuan. The cost of teacher training is not included. Such a huge amount is naturally not easy to raise.

This must be designed separately.

(IV) Methods for Out-of-School Adults to Enter School for Supplementary Education and to Train Teachers

A. The number of illiterate people nationwide who should receive supplementary education is estimated to be 202,435,277, and the number of literate people is 87,218,990, as mentioned above. It is only necessary for each literate person to teach two and a half people to achieve complete universalization. Therefore, a mandatory order should be issued to illiterate people to make them learn, and a mobilization order should be issued to literate people to make them teach others to read. Their obligation to teach others to read is as important as the obligation to serve in the military and pay taxes. However, it is impossible to divide these 202 million illiterate people equally among the 87 million literate people to teach them. Therefore, this plan is to use a class-based national literacy school and a non-class-based national literacy center to complement each other.

B. What is the difference between a national literacy school and a national literacy center? If there are illiterate people in families, small shops, and other small-scale organizational groups, they can be guided by literate members of the family, shop, or group, without taking class-based lessons.

This is called a national literacy center, which is assessed by nearby primary schools. Each center has one director and several teachers, who are additionally hired by the principals of nearby primary schools. National literacy schools are established in the military, factories, prisons, and all large institutions, or places where there are dozens or more illiterate people. Other illiterate people who do not enter national literacy schools must organize national literacy centers.

C. The teachers of national literacy schools are drawn from county-level senior primary schools,

county-level normal schools, provincial normal schools, senior high school normal departments, military academies, and all secondary schools and above, which set up classes to recruit all students from their respective schools, giving them at least three weeks of training, and also recruit private school teachers and give them two months of training, which can barely be applied. The sources of these teachers are estimated as follows (Note 6):

(1) Students from secondary schools and above: 220,000

(2) Private school teachers: at least 200,000

(3) Senior primary school students: 580,000

The above does not include primary school teachers. The reason is given in item B of the previous section. Among them, half or one-third of items (1) and (3) graduate from school every year. Therefore, although there are 800,000 people, only 500,000 people can actually serve as adult supplementary education teachers each year. Private school teachers cannot be fully used; selecting one-quarter of the excellent ones can yield about 50,000 people. Together, there are 550,000 people, which is about four times the estimated number of teachers needed in item B of the previous section, 135,000, which is enough to rotate. Furthermore, there is the method of national literacy in item D below to adjust and remedy, so in any case, it can always be sufficient.

D. Teachers of national literacy centers are filled by literate members of their own families, shops, and institutions, and can be divided into two types:

(1) Primary school students: 7,000,000

(2) Literate adults: 73,000,000 (Note 7)

The total of the above numbers is 80 million people. It is estimated that if these 80 million teachers each teach two people, they can educate 160 million people in four months.

Literacy center teachers are trained by primary schools and improved private schools. The training period is two months. In this way, literate people teach and those who need supplementary education learn. Literate people seem to receive national training together with illiterate people.

E. The Ministry of Education establishes a central national literacy instructor training institute, taking the capital's national literacy movement as a pilot and training center, recruiting students with a senior high school education or above, enrolling students in two sessions each year, 80 to 100 people each time, graduating every six months, and sending them to various provinces in succession for long-term guidance and responsible for assessing results. In this way, each province will gain an average of three full-time adult supplementary education workers every six months. After six years, each province will have more than 30 people, which will be very convenient when the second phase of the plan is carried out in the future.

Female athletes washing

Photographed by Lin Zeren of the Photography Society

(V) Ways to Increase School Building Equipment

For the implementation of national literacy training, the school buildings required, in addition to the small number of people in national literacy centers and easier planning, the national literacy schools, estimated according to item C of the third section, each school needs at least two rooms. In addition to those shared with primary schools, the national 1,915 counties need an average of 589 schools per county. In cities, of course, public institutions can be used.

Charitable institutions, secondary schools and above, are not easy to find in rural areas and small towns. Although the area of ​​pavilions is small, they can also be used. Although tea shops have business relations, they can also be borrowed for one or two hours. As a last resort, temples, open spaces, can be used in spring and autumn on sunny days. This is temporary. On the one hand, primary school buildings should be built in remote rural areas as soon as possible, and the ancestral temples and temples originally borrowed as school buildings should be given up as places for adult supplementary education. The equipment can also be borrowed from the original ones. If it is an empty room, students should bring their own seats. In addition, private donations of houses can be encouraged, or funds can be donated to build school buildings, or the government can raise funds to build simple public education halls or farmer education halls to run public literacy education.

(VI) Budget and Allocation of Funds

First, the budget for funds. The funds required for the implementation of adult supplementary education mentioned above is about 283.4 million yuan. This number is obtained from proportional calculation. How much is the exact amount? It is necessary to make a practical estimate as follows:

Budget for National Literacy Training Expenses

Subject Expenditure

First item: Implementation of National Literacy 56,587,440

Training expenses in yuan

The numbers listed above are the annual requirements.

First sub-item: Printing fee 3,706,100

First entry: Thousand-Character Textbook 168,70

Assuming each book is shared by two people, each book is used in three terms, and there are more than 224 million people, about 33.74 million books are needed in total. The printing fee for each book is 3 cents, totaling 1,012,200 yuan. Divided into six years, the annual requirement is about the above number.

Second sub-item: Public Weekly 2,700,000

Assuming each copy is shared by 30 people, about 6.75 million copies are needed. The printing fee for each copy is 1 cent per issue, 40 issues per year, totaling 4 jiao. The total requirement is about the above number.

Third sub-item: Literacy National Certificate 337,400

33.74 million people are trained each year, one copy per person, one cent per copy, totaling the above number.

Fourth sub-item: Patriotic Award Certificate 500,000

According to item D of section 4, there may be 80 million teachers in the public literacy center.

Assuming one-fifth of them are awarded each term, 16 million certificates should be prepared, 48 million certificates each year in three terms. Based on 50 million certificates, the printing fee for each certificate is 1 cent, totaling the above number.

Second item: Stationery fee 2,250,000

Assuming each set is used in three shifts, about 11.25 million sets are needed each year. Each set is 2 jiao, totaling about the above number.

Third item: Teacher salaries 33,741,000

According to the number of teachers in the National Literacy School in item B of section 3, there are 112,470 people. The average annual salary for each person is 300 yuan, totaling the above number.

Fourth item: Central National Literacy Guide 15,000

Member Training Fee

First entry: Recurring expenses 10,000

According to item E of section 4, the average training fee for each student is 100 yuan per year, totaling the above number.

Second entry: Start-up fee 5,000

The start-up fee totals 30,000 yuan, with an annual average requirement of the above number in six years.

Fifth item: Central National Literacy Guidance 660,000

Member Salary and Travel Expenses

The first half year is free. From the second half of the first year, there are 100 people, from the second year, there are 200 people, and from the second half of the third year, there are 300 people. The number increases accordingly.

100 yuan per person per month, totaling 3.96 million yuan for six years.

The annual average is the above number.

Sixth item: County and city training knowledge 1,149,000

Character teacher expenses

There are a total of 1,915 counties in the country, with an annual calculation of 600 yuan per county, totaling the above number.

Seventh item: School building expenses 5,623,500

No expenses are incurred for borrowing. However, according to the compulsory education plan, the repair and opening equipment fee is about 500 yuan per school. Borrowing tables and chairs or students preparing their own can reduce 200 yuan. Calculated at 300 yuan, 112,470 schools need a total of 33,741,000 yuan. The annual average fundraising in six years needs the above number.

Eighth item: Maintenance fee and miscellaneous expenses 6,748,200

Chalk, lighting, tea, office stationery, etc., 5 yuan per school per month.

The annual requirement is the above number.

Ninth item: Reserve fee 2,694,640

The reserve fee is calculated at 5% of the total of the first to eighth items listed above, requiring the above number.

Second, allocation of funds. The above budget can be considered a relatively accurate number (about 1.65 yuan per student per year, including teacher training, which is only 16% different from the estimated 1.4 yuan in item D of the previous section). In terms of nature, it is used to carry out local national literacy training, and it seems that the local government should bear it. However, according to the current financial situation of the local government, it is absolutely impossible to bear this cost completely. Therefore, it is appropriate for the central and local governments to share the burden.

Referring to the compulsory education example in Chapter 1, the sharing standard is formulated as follows:

Central government: Bears 45% of the total amount

Provincial government: Bears 10% of the total amount

County government: Bears 45% of the total amount

According to the above standards, the total amount borne by the central and local governments is as follows:

Central government: Should bear 25,464,348 yuan annually

Provincial government: Should bear 5,658,744 yuan annually

County government: Should bear 25,464,348 yuan annually

Total: 56,587,440 yuan

The number that the provincial government should raise, except for Tibet, Suiyuan, Rehe, Chahar, Ningxia, Xikang, Qinghai, and other six provinces, which have special circumstances and should be designed separately, if shared by the remaining 22 provinces such as Jiangsu, calculated, each province bears an average of more than 250,000 yuan per year. Also, the number that the county government should raise is temporarily allocated according to the current number of counties and cities in the country, 2,000 (Note 8). Each county should raise an average of more than 12,500 yuan per year. However, the population, financial resources, and environment of each county are different, so how can they be the same? Therefore, the number of counties to bear can also be assumed as in the table below:

First-class counties: 15,000 yuan to 25,000 yuan

Second-class counties: 5,000 yuan to 15,000 yuan

Third-class counties: Below 5,000 yuan

(VII) Methods for Editing National Literacy Teaching Materials

First, the Ministry of Education should compile a Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Textbook in the shortest possible time, so that ordinary people can complete it in four months, one hour per day.

Second, the textbook compiled in the previous article should use a mixed compilation method, with phonetic symbols attached to promote Mandarin Chinese. In addition to focusing on the Three Principles of the People, the teaching materials should also cover common sense.

Third, the Ministry of Education should edit the Public Weekly based on the vocabulary of the first book of the Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Textbook and 20% new words, so that those who have completed the first book of the Thousand-Character Textbook can easily read it.

Fourth, the Ministry of Education should edit the Public Series of Books based on the vocabulary of the Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Textbook and 20% new words.

Fifth, the above publications are allowed to be reprinted by bookstores nationwide, and the price should be extremely low.

(VIII) Procedures for Implementing Universalization

First, organize specialized responsible agencies. Before implementing compulsory education, each county and city should first organize a National Literacy Training Committee and branches, as well as offices, etc., as specialized responsible agencies. The system is as follows:

County: Committee, District: Branch, Township or Town: Branch, Hamlet: Office, At least one office per hamlet.

The organization of each association and office, as well as the selection of committee members, are shown in the table below:

County Committee District Branch Township or Town Branch Hamlet Office

County Education Bureau Chief District Chief Township Chief or Town Chief Hamlet Chief

One representative of the County Chief One representative of the District Education Association One representative of the District Education Association Appointed by the Hamlet Chief

One representative of the County Education Bureau One representative of the District Party Department Representatives jointly recommended by each district branch in the district Two literate people from the hamlet

Appointed by the Education Bureau, one to three people who are enthusiastic about national literacy training Appointed by the District Chief, two people who are enthusiastic about national literacy training Appointed by the Township Chief or Town Chief, two people who are enthusiastic about national literacy training

A total of five to seven people A total of five people A total of five people A total of three people

The above associations and offices, except in special circumstances, should all be established before the scheduled implementation period in each locality and reported to the Provincial Department of Education for record. In places where the district, township, and town system has not yet been implemented, the city and township directors and village chiefs may be temporarily responsible.

Second, conduct surveys in stages. After the establishment of the above agencies, conduct implementation surveys. The targets of the survey are two:

A. The number and names of teachers in the district.

B. The names, addresses, and total number of illiterate people in the district.

The survey should be conducted in the following order:

(1) Survey starts from the hamlet, the hamlet chief should investigate and register two copies two and a half months before the local implementation period, one to be submitted to the township or town branch, and one to be kept in the hamlet.

(2) The township or town branch must compile the reports from each hamlet two months before the local implementation period and prepare a concise summary report in two copies, one to be submitted to the district branch and one to be kept in the township or town.

(3) The district branch must compile the reports from each subordinate township and town one and a half months before the local implementation period and prepare a concise summary report in two copies,

one to be submitted to the county committee and one to be kept in the district.

(4) The county committee must compile the reports from each subordinate district one month before the county implementation period and prepare a concise summary report in two copies, one to be submitted to the Provincial Department of Education and one to be kept in the committee.

Third, allocate teachers and students and notify them separately.

A. One month before the compulsory implementation period, all hamlets should mobilize simultaneously.

Except for places where the number of students is over fifty, which is enough to set up a school, a school should be set up immediately. For those who cannot set up a school, the names of teachers and students should be allocated one by one according to the standard of one teacher for every three students.

Issue a notice and announce it in the hamlet.

B. If there are not enough teachers, the upper-level branch may be requested to dispatch qualified teachers for assistance.

C. Those who have the obligation to teach may be exempted from their obligation if they have special circumstances and are certified by the head of the agency or the hamlet chief, but they must pay a donation of three yuan for teaching literacy to be deposited in the hamlet office as the cost of hiring someone to teach in their place.

D. If there is a surplus of teachers in the hamlet, the hamlet office should register the names and addresses of the surplus teachers and report them to the township and town branch for dispatch to other hamlets where there is a shortage of teachers.

E. Distribute the supplies separately.

9. Scheduled Compulsory Period and Post-Compulsory Assessment

First, an order was issued on July 1, 1919 of the Republic of China, announcing to the national public that the Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Textbook must be completed before the end of December of the 25th year. A second announcement was issued on September 1.

Second, compulsory implementation began in cities, towns, and villages on January 1, 1920 of the Republic of China.

Third, compulsory implementation began in the provincial capitals, cities, towns, and villages of each province on January 1, 1921 of the Republic of China.

Fourth, compulsory implementation began in the cities, towns, and villages of first-class and second-class counties on January 1, 1923 of the Republic of China.

Fifth, compulsory implementation began in the cities, towns, and villages of third-class counties on January 1, 1925 of the Republic of China. (To be continued)

Last Night

German Industrial Delegation Arrives in Shanghai

Will Enter Beijing Within a Few Days

German Minister Also Arrives Today

The German industrial delegation of eight people, invited by the National Government to come to China for inspection, inspected Guangzhou for a week and then took the German mail ship Telflinger of Mei Zuishi Foreign Company from Hong Kong on the 10th to Shanghai. They arrived in port at 10 o'clock last night. The ship docked at the Gonghexing Wharf in Hongkou. After all the members of the delegation landed, they stayed at the Hua Mao Hotel on the Bund of Nanjing Road. The Chinese agencies that went to the boat to welcome them last night included Xu Shanxiang, representative of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Yang Gongzhao, representative of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines, Zhang Yunhai, representative of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Zhu Chongguang, representative of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Shen Yi, Xu Peihuang, representatives of the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, Hu Shuhua, representative of Tongji University, and Tan Boyu. The Shanghai Special Municipal Government has scheduled a banquet this afternoon to welcome all the members of the delegation and introduce the two sides to meet.

The formal public banquet will be held after the delegation goes to Beijing and returns to Shanghai at a later date.

Mission to China, a reporter from this newspaper visited the delegation at the Hua Mao Hotel last night and was met by the head of the delegation, Mr. Le Ciman.

He told the reporter that his mission to China was that he had been in China for more than 20 years and returned to Germany seven years ago. He was very happy to revisit the old place. The German industrial inspection delegation is purely composed of representatives of important industrial circles in Germany. The motivation for their visit to China

originated when Sun Ke, Minister of Railways of the National Government, visited Germany two years ago. At that time, Minister Sun had contacted the German industrial delegation and welcomed the German industrial circles to invest in China to develop various industries in China, so as to seek cooperation between the economic circles of China and Germany. After Minister Sun returned to China, he sent a telegram on behalf of the National Government, formally inviting the German industrial circles to organize a delegation to China to observe the economic and industrial conditions in South China

and North China, and then formulate a development plan.

Consult with each other before investing. He believes that the only prerequisite for industrial development is peace.

They plan to stay in Shanghai for a few days to inspect the industrial and economic conditions in Shanghai, and then officially enter Beijing. However, the date of entering Beijing has not yet been determined, approximately no later than this week or the beginning of next week. After visiting the government authorities in Beijing, they will come to Shanghai again. The inspection plan after this must be determined by the government. However, their planned inspection itinerary is to first go to Wuxi. He and Mr. Rong, a giant of Wuxi industry, are very familiar. Then they will go up the Yangtze River to Daye, Hankou, Changsha, and other places, and then return to Shanghai and go north. They are also preparing to inspect Taiyuan. Unfortunately, the north and south are currently in opposition. Whether the government will allow them to go to Taiyuan has not yet been determined. In addition, they plan to go to Tianjin, Beiping, and various places in the three northeastern provinces for inspection, and then return to Shanghai and return to the country.

Organization of the delegation. The delegation was established in February this year. On February 28, they took the Japanese mail ship Hakone Maru from Wusai Port and set out for China. They arrived in Hong Kong on March 30, transferred to Guangzhou, and took the Telflinger German mail ship from Hong Kong on the 7th to Shanghai. They arrived in port last night. There are a total of eight members of the delegation as follows: (1)

Head of the delegation, Mr. Le Ciman, is a factory manager, director, and representative of the board of directors. He was the chief member of the German Industrial Association, president of the Keseng Industrial Association, and a member of the German Industrial Association. (2) Professor Tetuo Ma is a representative of the German electrical industry and a professor at the Industrial Higher School. He was engaged in the design work of the Soviet Russian government's power industry construction and has written extensively. (3) Winter, PhD, is a representative of German industry. He was the director of the Krupp factory and the president of the German Engineering Society. (4) Leitma is a representative of the civil engineering industry. He is currently a senior German railway architect and participated in the construction of the Jinpu Railway in China. (5) Gentaite is a representative of the German machine industry. quite experienced. (7) Xuber is a representative of the German Central Bank. His main purpose in coming to China is to investigate China's financial and economic situation and improve the currency system. (8) Shi Quliu is the secretary of the delegation.

Social Bureau

Proclamation to Maintain People's Food Supply

Rice Merchants Ordered to Suppress Prices to Eighteen Yuan

Rice Shops Ordered to Reduce Selling Prices Again

According to a report from the Wuchen Society, rice arriving in southern Shanghai yesterday has not ceased. Sales of Jiangsu and Tongbai japonica rice are relatively smooth, with the price falling by one dime. Songjiang's thin rice paddy, due to its weakened digestion, also dropped by a dime. The asking prices of other Qingjiao thin rice paddy and Changbang japonica rice are lower than the previous day. If clear weather brings a rush of goods, the rice market can stabilize, preventing further changes. However, foreign rice is still rising strongly, as inland purchases are very active.

Procurement in Ningbo and Wenzhou is particularly urgent. The Zhabei rice market has become lively, with over 3,000 shi sold yesterday, and prices have fallen by half a dime. Top-grade Qingpu thin rice paddy is selling for nineteen yuan. However, the prices published in newspapers do not specify grades or sources, resulting in a difference of one or several yuan compared to the southern market. The Social Bureau is deeply concerned that some people are obscuring the situation and raising prices. Yesterday, it ordered the Bean and Rice Trade Association, the Shanghai Northern Rice Grain Sales Association, and the Jiagutang Rice Industry Association to advise their members not to raise prices again during this period of falling rice prices and to find ways to lower them further. The highest price for top-grade japonica rice is set at

eighteen yuan. Furthermore, as flour is an essential supplementary food, yesterday, the Flour Mill Association was instructed to inform its members not to take advantage of the situation by raising prices or monopolizing goods. The bureau also reported that the Zhabei Rice Grain Sales Association reported that rice boats transporting rice from Wangting to Shanghai were detained in Suzhou. A request was submitted to the mayor to forward a letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to negotiate the matter. Details of the entire text and the negotiations regarding the detained rice are recorded below:

Order to the Bean and Rice Trade Association and the Sales Association, to be obeyed. According to today's newspaper, boat owner Ding Fugen of the Zhabei rice market is asking nineteen yuan for his thin rice paddy. In addition, the lowest price of the four households of Zhang, Tang, Xu, and Song is also eighteen yuan. Furthermore, boat owner Hua Zuozhou is asking nineteen yuan and forty-five cents for ordinary japonica rice, while the other two households of Ding and Pei are also asking above nineteen yuan and twenty-five cents. However, the highest price of japonica rice in the southern Shanghai rice market is seventeen yuan and eighty cents, and the highest price of thin rice paddy is seventeen yuan and seventy cents. Within the same region, on the same day, the northern and southern

rice markets are so disparate as to be alarming. Even if the quality of the rice is superior, a slightly higher price should be stated to avoid shaking the market.

Moreover, generalizing as "ordinary japonica rice" without distinguishing sources and grades is even more likely to breed misunderstandings and lead to the clandestine sale of top-grade japonica rice at high prices. Such a lack of distinction between high and low grades clearly has the drawback of undermining price limits and should be strictly admonished to serve as a warning. If there is no repentance, severe punishment will be given. You are to immediately inform all merchants and boat owners to comply.

As for top-grade japonica rice, the price limit of eighteen yuan should have been in effect from the eighth. However, representatives Ye Huijun and Jiang Shizhi from the association came to the bureau to explain their difficulties, which seemed genuine. A few more days will be granted.

You are still instructed to find ways to lower prices immediately. The highest price for top-grade japonica rice is eighteen yuan, and other rice types should not delay and wait,

intending to test the waters, which would be inconvenient. This is a strict order.

Order to the Jiagutang Public Office, to be obeyed. According to today's newspaper, members of the office are publicly discussing rice prices, with special japonica rice priced at twenty yuan, and the first and second grades of rice are all above nineteen yuan. Recent rice prices have gradually declined, and you, Ye, should lower prices accordingly based on the overall market. How can you still ask prices based on the rice market several days ago? This special order instructs the public office to fairly set prices for sale by referring to the current market to benefit the people's food supply and not to deliberately raise prices and hinder the livelihoods of ordinary people. You are also instructed to truthfully submit the prices of the special, first, second, and third grades of japonica rice for March for review. This order.

Order to the Flour Mill Association, to be obeyed. In recent times, rice prices have soared, causing panic among the people. This bureau is prepared to consider the commercial situation and people's livelihoods and provide proper maintenance. The rice market has recently stabilized, and people's hearts have been somewhat calmed. However, due to the thinness of grain production, people still feel difficulties with their food supply. As flour is an essential supplementary food, there is still fear that a few merchants, seeing the high price of rice, will take the opportunity to raise prices or monopolize goods, hoping to profit, which would hinder the people's food supply and endanger security. You are immediately ordered to inform your members to share the difficulties of the times, find ways to increase supply, and sell at fair prices, and not to engage in the aforementioned situations, which would lead to investigation. This order.

Negotiations on Detained Rice in Wangting: The Social Bureau reported that the Zhabei Rice Grain Sales Association reported that its member Long Hongji was transporting rice from Wangting to Shanghai and was detained by the Suzhou Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team. Similar situations have also been reported. It is said that Suzhou's detention of rice boats transporting rice to Shanghai is not a one-time occurrence. At this time of poor rice production, everyone feels that the people's food supply is insufficient. It depends on whether neighboring areas can communicate with each other, help each other in times of emergency, and overcome difficulties together. Now, the inland areas ignore the food supply of this city and treat it as an enemy country, repeatedly stopping rice sales. If the city is unable to make up for the shortage of inland rice supply and is forced to ban the export of foreign rice to ensure its own survival, what will be the panic of the inland people's food supply? These situations have been reported to Mayor Zhang, who has forwarded a letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to pay attention, determine a mutually supportive and coexisting approach, and immediately

release the detained rice boats heading to Shanghai.

Overseas Chinese from Southeast Asia

An Appeal to Eliminate Private Postal Bureaus

Various organizations in Singapore are sending letters and telegrams, exerting every effort to appeal for the elimination of private postal bureaus (Minxinju) by both Chinese and foreign authorities. A summary of these appeals is as follows:

Urgent Telegram on Behalf of Various Organizations, to the Central Party Headquarters, National Government, Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, Shanghai Overseas Chinese United Association, National Federation of Commerce, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Overseas Chinese Advancement Association, National Chambers of Commerce, Newspaper Offices, and Community Organizations. Published in the Shanghai Shen Bao, February 28th. The Director-General of the Postal Administration of the Ministry of Communications, in a statement to a reporter from the Guomin News Agency, regarding the issue of private postal bureaus in Nanyang (Southeast Asia) handling general package delivery, is deceiving overseas Chinese and misleading the Chinese people. Upon reading this, we are deeply saddened. We hereby list the details of the petition to eliminate private postal bureaus and increase postal rates, along with the background, and refute the statement as follows: (1) The Director-General of the Postal Administration stated that in August of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the postal administration of British Malaya in Kuala Lumpur sent a telegram stating that the governments of the Malay Peninsula and various islands in Nanyang had decided to abolish the private postal bureau system and would implement it on January 1st of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), and that a letter was sent on September 2nd reiterating the request for abolition, etc. As such, it seems that the abolition of private postal bureaus originated from the British territory.

However, the true facts are quite different. In October of the 15th year of the Republic (1926), the Ministry of Communications in Beijing had once issued an order to abolish private postal packages, but after the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce, representing all overseas Chinese, appealed to the Chinese and foreign authorities, it was granted an indefinite extension. Subsequently, after the unification of the North in the 17th year of the Republic (1928) and the establishment of our National Government, in November, the Shantou Postal Bureau suddenly issued new regulations prohibiting private postal bureaus from sending or receiving general packages via mail. On February 26th of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the Chamber of Commerce again strongly argued based on the previous case, and on April 23rd, they received Approval No. 65 from the Ministry of Communications, which stated, in brief, that private postal bureaus should not exist permanently, nor was an indefinite extension necessary, thus overturning the established case.

This aroused outrage among overseas Chinese. On July 13th, a general meeting of all overseas Chinese was convened in the Chamber of Commerce, unanimously advocating for continued petitions, with letters and telegrams being sent back and forth, repeatedly appealing the decision. The news spread, prompting local governments to pay extra attention. The Secretary for Chinese Affairs repeatedly inquired with the directors of the Chamber of Commerce. If the Ministry of Communications had not issued a directive stating that private postal bureaus should not exist and should be abolished, there would have been no general meeting of all overseas Chinese, nor would it have aroused the suspicion of the local government. Where did the telegrams and letters from the Kuala Lumpur Postal Administration in August and September originate? It is not hard to imagine. The facts are clear and documented. Who would believe that it did not originate from our own country? (2) This can also be proven by the petition presented by the "Singapore Overseas Chinese General Meeting for Petitioning to Retain Private Postal Bureaus" on October 13th of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), which stated, in part, that "Postal bureaus in Singapore, Malacca, and other places that require private postal bureaus to obtain licenses for operation have recently expired and are said to be ceasing to renew them,

and upon inquiring about the reasons, they cite the fact that our country's postal service has already abolished private postal bureaus as a reason, and state that if our government still agrees to retain them, there would be no problem on their end and licenses would definitely be issued as before." However, the Ministry of Communications has not provided any reply or explanation to this, further increasing the confusion among overseas Chinese. It was not until the representatives met with the Governor of Singapore that they learned that the Director-General of the Postal Administration had taken the initiative to correspond with the Postmaster General of Kuala Lumpur to discuss the abolition, and the overseas Chinese then realized the reason for the Ministry of Communications' lack of response and explanation. (3) This year, when representatives met with the Governor of Singapore to petition for a reduction in fees, the Postmaster General of Kuala Lumpur was also present and presented a letter from the Director-General of our country's Postal Administration, which included (1) requesting the Postmaster General of Kuala Lumpur to cease renewing licenses for private postal bureaus in Singapore and other places in 1930, (2) stating that a commissioner had been appointed to order private postal bureaus in Shantou and Xiamen to send overseas letters and affix postage stamps of one cent according to regulations, (3) stating that the joint postal system would definitely be able to be practically implemented. According to the letter, he spoke grandly,

directly claiming to be in compliance with the international postal convention. However, what is incomprehensible is that while he requested the Postmaster General of Kuala Lumpur to stop issuing licenses to private postal bureaus in 1930, he embellished his words when talking to reporters, saying that his goal was to ensure that the communication of overseas Chinese would not be inconvenienced by the abolition of private postal bureaus by the British postal service. This is contradictory and self-deceptive. If licenses are stopped, private postal bureaus will be closed, so how can communication be made convenient for overseas Chinese? Moreover, if the joint postal system is to be implemented, fundamental planning for postal services should also be initiated. Is transportation convenient in the provinces of Fujian and Guangdong? Has the population been registered? Are there post offices in remote rural areas? Are bandits rampant everywhere? Has the Director-General of the Postal Administration considered this? If he only focuses on increasing fees, claiming that this would both avoid criticism for not complying with the international postal convention and increase postal revenue, while ignoring the suffering of overseas Chinese and disregarding their earnest pleas, is this the attitude that a communications authority that claims to care for overseas Chinese and facilitate the public should have? Based on the above three points, the situation is already clear.

Yet the Director-General of the Postal Administration claims that it "runs counter to the facts." On what basis does he say this? If he claims to have sent a telegram to the British authorities to inquire, then the British authorities must have replied. He should present the original text of the correspondence to clarify the truth. Otherwise, he will be guilty of harming the country and the people. The overseas Chinese feel deeply pained as their families' lives depend on this. Now that there is no way to appeal, we are again presenting the details and tearfully requesting our Central Party Headquarters

and the National Government to uphold Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, earnestly protect overseas Chinese, and alleviate their suffering. We also hope that our compatriots in the country will sympathize with the difficulties of overseas Chinese and unite to protest, awaiting your urgent command.

Singapore Organizations Petitioning for the Reduction of Private Postal Fees, Overseas Chinese General Meeting, respectfully presented by Delegation Chairman Lin Jin Dian.

March 15th, Year 19 of the Republic.

An Open Letter to Compatriots at Home and Abroad,

Respectfully submitted,

Last May, our Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce received a directive from the Ministry of Communications stating that private postal bureaus should not exist permanently and that there was no need for an indefinite extension.

Page 14

Upon hearing this, our overseas Chinese were deeply troubled and rushed about. Overseas and domestic private postal bureaus are intrinsically linked, serving as a major institution needed by overseas Chinese to send money and letters to support their families. If private postal bureaus in Shantou and Xiamen are forced to close, overseas private postal bureaus will also have to close simultaneously. Although post offices can be used for communication,

the lack of convenience would be difficult for overseas Chinese to bear. Therefore, we petitioned for their retention. We were deeply grateful when the Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Communications to temporarily suspend the measure. However, last year, the Postal Administration suddenly appointed officials to order private postal bureaus in Shantou and Xiamen to affix postage stamps of one cent to each letter sent overseas. At the same time, the local government

also began to abolish them, requiring each letter to have a postage stamp of one cent and two cents affixed. According to the usual rates for private postal letters, each letter sent abroad costs three cents, and each general package of forty letters sent domestically costs twenty-eight cents. Now, both governments are requiring adherence to the postal regulations, which is too heavy a burden and causes great suffering to our people. However, when elected representatives approached the local government to request a reduction, they were told that the abolition and increased fees were advocated by our government. What are the intentions of the ruling officials? We overseas Chinese are ignorant and dare not speculate.

Because the local government is implementing the fee increase, scheduled for April 1st, the lighterage industry association was compelled to appeal. Sixty-three organizations participated, holding a general meeting of overseas Chinese at the Chinese Chamber of Commerce on the 23rd of last month. The attendees were crowded, unanimously advocating for continued petitions, and immediately

established the "Singapore Organizations Petitioning for Reduction of Private Postal Fees, Overseas Chinese General Meeting." On one hand, we earnestly requested the local government for a four-month extension to allow for discussion and negotiation. On the other hand, we publicly nominated Mr. Lu Weisheng, a member of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of the Central Government, as the petition representative. Over the past few days, over fifty telegrams have been sent from various clan associations, community organizations, the Malacca Chinese Chamber of Commerce, and the Singapore Overseas Chinese General Meeting,

but all have been ignored. Overseas Chinese have always loved their country and contributed funds, not wanting to be outdone by others. The facts are all there and should be trusted by compatriots throughout the country. We have secretly hoped that after unification, everything would be renewed, and the suffering previously experienced by overseas Chinese might be alleviated once and for all. But now, the suffering is compounded and the pain intensified, the opposite of what we expected, which is beyond our expectations. If the abolition of private postal bureaus is intended to comply with international postal conventions, then the fundamental task is to facilitate transportation, register the population, and eliminate bandits. Only then can what is taken from the people also benefit the people. Now, without attending to these tasks, the remittances of overseas Chinese still rely on private postal bureaus for delivery, and labor costs must inevitably be subsidized, resulting in a double burden. How can countless laborers, who toil like oxen and barely earn a meager sum of sweat and blood to support their families, endure this? Now, with exhausted strength and hoarse voices, we must remotely appeal to various newspapers, community organizations, and compatriots at home and abroad to unite and strive to have the Ministry of Communications withdraw its decision and handle matters as before. In addition to sending a telegram on this day, we are also submitting a letter

to request that you investigate and appeal on our behalf. We cannot express our sincere plea enough. With best wishes.

Singapore Organizations Petitioning for Reduction of Private Postal Fees, Overseas Chinese General Meeting,

Delegation Chairman Lin Jin Dian, March 15th, Year 19 of the Republic.

Petition from Various Organizations, To His Excellency Sir Clementi, Governor and Commander-in-Chief of the Straits Settlements. The petitioners Lin Jin Dian, Li Jin Ci, Luo Cheng De, Wang Sheng Shi, Zhuang Du Ding, Tang Xiang Lin, Huang Qin Sheng, et al., respectfully submit the following: (1) Overseas Chinese in this locality who send money and letters to their families in rural areas of mainland China generally do so using the general package method. That is, the remitter hands over the money and letters to their families to the local private postal bureau. The private postal bureau assembles hundreds or thousands of similar letters into a general package. Each letter in the general package pays a postage fee of three cents, which the post office then forwards to its branch offices on the Chinese coast. After delivery, the branch office then distributes the money and letters to the recipients in various inland villages and towns, while collecting return letters or receipts, which are assembled into a general package and sent back to the local private postal bureau. (2) Last year, the Chinese government indicated its intention to abolish the private postal bureau system. Overseas Chinese in this locality,

held a general meeting at the Chinese Chamber of Commerce and elected representatives to petition the National Government. As a result, the National Government agreed to allow private postal bureaus to continue operating as before.

(3) At the end of last year, the Secretary for Chinese Affairs of this locality notified us that the local government would increase the postage fee for general packages from three cents per letter to the standard fee of one cent and two cents per letter. (4) After receiving the notification, the committee immediately appointed four representatives to meet with the Acting Governor of Singapore on January 20, 1930. They learned that the local government would not allow the postage fee to remain the same. The delegation then explained in detail that the Chinese postal service was not yet sufficiently developed and could not replace the private postal bureaus in delivering money and letters in inland villages and towns. Therefore, private postal bureaus are currently the only affordable and convenient method for communication and money transfer for the working-class overseas Chinese community. The Acting Governor told the delegation that the local government's abolition of private postal bureaus,

was based on the request of the Chinese postal authorities. (5) On February 1, 1930, Report No. 277, carried by the local newspapers, reported that the postage fee for general packages would be one cent and two cents per letter, to be implemented after March 31, 1930. According to the report, in addition to the fee increase, the government has agreed to retain the private postal bureaus, which means that the local government has realized that there is no better method to replace private postal bureaus, so the existence of private postal bureaus at present is indispensable. (6) On February 25, 1930,

Sixty-three public organizations and associations in this locality held a joint meeting again at the Chinese Chamber of Commerce. We were elected as committee members to petition Your Excellency to extend the order to increase the postage fee for general packages by four months from March 31, 1930. (7) The purpose of requesting an extension is to allow us sufficient time to send representatives to petition our National Government,

as we know that the current Chinese postal service cannot replace the private postal bureaus in delivering money and letters. We believe that the Chinese government has ordered the retention of private postal bureaus, and we have explained the difficulties to the British government,

and stated that the proposal to abolish private postal bureaus originated from the British government. We believe that the communications between the local government and the Chinese government must be the result of some misunderstanding. (8) If we can obtain a direct

statement from the Chinese government that private postal bureaus cannot be abolished at present, we believe that the local government will not forcibly increase the postage fee. We believe that as long as private postal bureaus exist, there is no sufficient reason to increase the postage fee during the period when they are obligated to perform the delivery duties on behalf of the postal service. We have stated that the general package method involves thousands of letters in one package. Now, the post office wants to forcibly increase the postage fee for each letter in the general package. Isn't this forcing the working-class overseas Chinese community to pay the same fee for distributing thousands of letters and collecting thousands of return letters as for simply delivering one general package? We believe that the government's treatment of the working-class community is extremely unfair. (9) We know that the remittance rate charged by private postal bureaus is often higher than the market rate. If the post office can remit a few dollars at the market rate, the increase in postage fee would not be a problem, as the lower remittance rate would compensate for the loss. Now, the post office is increasing the postage fee without undertaking the delivery duties, and making the working-class overseas Chinese, who send two or three dollars per month, pay one cent and two cents to the local post office, as well as the return letter fee to the Chinese post office, and also suffer the loss from the remittance rate charged by private postal bureaus. We dare say that the total amount of these expenses is unbearable for the impoverished working-class community. We respectfully request Your Excellency to extend the order to increase the postage fee for general packages by four months. We await your decision.

Singapore Organizations Petitioning for Reduction of Private Postal Fees, Delegation. March 4th, Year 19 of the Republic.

Telephone Service in the Concessions

Contents of the Special Operating Conditions

Revised Prices Must Be Agreed Upon

A Central Exchange to Be Established in the French Concession

According to the Zi Lin Daily, the special operating conditions for telephone service in the concessions were agreed upon by the Public Works Department and the Council of the French Concession last week and sent to the China and Foreign Telephone Company on Saturday. They have now been distributed to the Telephone Advisory Committee and various companies interested in acquiring the company for consideration. The special operating term is set for forty years in the first phase, starting from April 1st of this year, followed by a ten-year term thereafter. However, a notice must be given two years in advance for mutual consultation. The same applies if the municipal authorities want to acquire the company.

The most noteworthy aspect of the new conditions is the cancellation of Article 15 of the old conditions regarding the use of stock premium income for public reserve funds, which is replaced by a public utility tax. It stipulates that the telephone fee for municipal authorities be reduced by 20% for the first five years. From the sixth to the tenth year, the aforementioned discount is canceled, and the company will contribute 2.5% of the total revenue from users in both concessions

to the municipal authorities according to the revenue ratio of each concession. From the eleventh year onwards, the contribution should be increased to 5%. Regarding telephone fees, it is stipulated that the current prices will be maintained until the full implementation of automatic telephones. If prices are revised in the future, it should be agreed upon by both the company and the municipal authorities, and the pricing standard should be based on obtaining a certain percentage of net profit on the total invested capital. If the annual net profit exceeds the specified percentage, half of the excess will go to the company and half will be allocated to a provisional account for revised prices. If the net profit in a certain year is less than the specified percentage due to reasons beyond human control, funds will be allocated from the account to make up the difference. Each time prices are revised, the balance of this account should be used as a standard for increase or decrease. The current practice of reducing telephone fees by 20% for shareholders with four or more shares has also been canceled. It is also stipulated that a central exchange should be established in the French Concession by the end of March 1934, and more should be added as appropriate, so that the French Concession has an independent telephone network with first-class service and good connections with the Public Concession and Nanshi. There is also a limit to the number of telephone lines installed in the sky on the roads. According to a report in the Wenhui Daily, the new special operating conditions for telephone service are expected to be submitted to the annual meeting of Western taxpayers on the 16th of this month.

Unfortunate Events in the Shipping Industry

The "Tunan" Vehicle Disappears. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Tunan" ship was ordered to sail to Yingkou. As the items on board had not yet been unloaded and the ship was waiting for a certain cargo shipment to Beijing, it had been in Yingkou for many days. Yesterday, the company received an urgent telegram from Yingkou stating that the marine engineer of the "Tunan" ship, A. P. Cranston, had suddenly disappeared. A thorough search was conducted, but he was nowhere to be found. All of his personal belongings on the ship had been taken away. His whereabouts were unknown. After receiving the telegram, the company immediately inquired with Mr. Warren, the Western chief of the engine department, asking if he had received a telegram from Mr. Cranston beforehand. According to Mr. Warren, he had not received any telegrams from Mr. Cranston after the "Tunan" arrived in Yingkou. The Shanghai office has replied to Mr. Huang Hongqian, the shipowner of the "Tunan," ordering him to quickly inquire about Mr. Cranston's whereabouts. At the same time, a telegram was sent to the Yingkou branch manager, instructing him to assist the "Tunan" in searching for the engineer's whereabouts in the vicinity. According to reports, Mr. Cranston is a British national who has worked as a crew member for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for 25 years and has been the chief engineer (i.e., marine engineer) of the "Tunan" for 17 years. His current monthly salary is 536 yuan. He has no mental illness. The Shanghai office believes that Mr. Cranston's disappearance is likely due to him leaving the ship on his own and is definitely not a life-threatening disappearance.

"Jiang'an" Collides with "Chutai". The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Jiang'an" ship, which came to Shanghai from Hankou, collided with a pontoon at Zhenjiang at 12:00 midnight on the 7th. At that time, the wind was strong and the water was turbulent. The naval warship "Chutai" was also moored outside the pontoon. As the "Jiang'an" ship was docking, it was impacted by the wind and waves, causing the ship to collide with the stern of the "Chutai," breaking the "Chutai's" stern mast.

The lights and cables on the stern were also damaged, and the hull sustained minor damage. After the "Jiang'an" ship returned to Shanghai yesterday, the mast was first removed to compensate "Chutai." Mr. Huang was also sent to Zhenjiang to inspect the damage to "Chutai" and arrange for repairs.

"Huayang" Worker Injured in Fall. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Huayang" ship was unloading cargo at the Jinliyuan Wharf yesterday. After clearing the hold, a dockworker wanted to retrieve goods from the bottom of the hold. Accidentally, he fell from the deck into the bottom of the hold. The dockworker was seriously injured. The water police sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that his life is in danger.

Proposal to Eliminate Odd-Numbered Weights and Sampling Practices in the Silk Industry

Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association, Silk Guild,

The following is the document issued on the 9th, as the association has resolved to regulate odd-numbered weights, eliminate the habit of wiping away fractions, and address the issue of foreign firms drawing excessive silk samples. It was sent to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau and the Foreign Silk Exporters' Association, requesting them to impartially correct these practices and inform all foreign firms to strictly comply. The original text of the two letters is recorded below.

Letter to the Commodity Inspection Bureau, Respectfully submitted, On the 5th of this month, Bao Tai and twelve other silk factories proposed to regulate the minimum unit of odd-numbered weights to maintain their interests. In the past, foreign firms would arbitrarily wipe out four or five tenths of a pound when weighing silk from factories, leading to disputes. Now that the Inspection Bureau is implementing public weighing, there is no need for foreign firms to weigh the silk. The Inspection Bureau should convert the public weight of pounds into catties to prevent foreign firms from arbitrarily wiping out fractions,

and to avoid the factories' past hidden losses. According to Japanese practice, fractions are wiped out in units of two and a half tenths. When calculating the portions, the Inspection Bureau should

convert the pounds into catties and notify the foreign firms, which will directly avoid unnecessary disputes and indirectly protect the interests of the factories. We request that you publicly decide on a method, etc. After public discussion, it was agreed that the proposal was indeed insightful and that fair trade should not be biased in any way. How can the public weight be arbitrarily wiped out? If this malpractice is not eliminated,

it will only lead to more disputes and excessive exploitation of the interests of silk merchants. The Bureau should take charge and approve the annotation of the pound and catty figures on the inspection certificate in the future, and notify all foreign firms that all habits of wiping out fractions

should follow the Japanese precedent, using four taels as a unit (i.e., two and a half tenths). Do not arbitrarily deduct them to resolve disputes and maintain fairness. In addition to the public resolution, this letter is hereby submitted to the Bureau, requesting that you investigate and handle the matter, and notify the buying foreign firms to comply. Please reply for our information.

Letter to the Foreign Silk Exporters' Association, Respectfully submitted, According to reports from our colleagues after the implementation of public weighing and inspection, the exporters have not implemented the seller's clauses agreed upon in your Association's letter of March 19th. After public discussion on April 5th,

the following resolutions were made: (A) Use canvas bags and immediately abolish all oil paper white lists. Each factory has the right to freely reform this. Exporters should no longer ask the seller to provide these abolished products or their value. Sellers already bear 23 taels and 3 mace for the packaging fee for every ten pieces of silk, so they should not make exceptions and demand them. If you believe that the previous oil paper white lists are necessary for the seller to supply, please provide a detailed breakdown of the packaging expenses. (B) Sample silks should be drawn according to the previous resolution, two strands for every five pieces. (C) The drawn strands should be given a receipt by the exporters, stating the number of strands and weight. When the strands are returned,

they should still be weighed and counted. (Weicheng Company was the first to implement this.

Recently, Junsheng, Fuxiang, Sheng and other factories delivered silk to Weicheng.

Weicheng signed a receipt for the drawn samples, stating the number of strands and weight). (D) For silk packages shipped on Saturdays, the silk payment should be made before noon on that day. (E) Please return all excessively taken samples of silk from April 1st. All of the above clauses are matters discussed in previous meetings. At the beginning of the reform, they have not been thoroughly implemented. Please impartially correct these practices and immediately investigate and implement them to prevent unexpected disputes. Please reply for our information.

Recent Disaster Situation in Henan and Shaanxi Provinces

Henan Disaster Victims Sitting and Waiting for Death

Shaanxi Disaster Victims Killing and Eating People

The unprecedented disaster in the Northwest, with its terrible situation and vast affected area, is truly unprecedented in history. The Relief Bureau has recently received urgent telegrams from Henan and Shaanxi provinces regarding the latest disaster situation, which are unbearable to read. Excerpts from the original telegrams are as follows: (A) Telegrams from the Henan Relief Bureau: (First Telegram) The disaster situation in Henan is intensifying.

In the western counties of Henan, hundreds of people are dying every day. In Shaanxi, Luoyang, Zhengzhou, and Kaifeng, over 50,000 people have already been taken in, and those being sent across the river for resettlement are still continuously arriving. Our bureau's relief funds are exhausted, and there is no way to raise more. Not to mention the starving people in the disaster areas who are waiting for death, even the 50,000 people we have taken in are on the verge of running out of food. Once they are dispersed, not only will transportation be disrupted, but there will also be no funds to send them away. It is estimated that there will be new wheat to eat in two months, but it will cost two yuan per person per month, about 200,000 yuan, to keep these 50,000 people alive. Although there are military operations now, they do not hinder the progress of relief. We earnestly request all groups to quickly provide assistance, in accordance with the principle of saving people thoroughly. (The rest is omitted.) (Second Telegram) Following the previous telegram, Henan Province is unfortunately caught in the war zone again. Transportation is blocked, and the lifeline is cut off. Shaanxi, Luoyang, Bianliang,

Zhengzhou, Qin, Bo, Meng, Xin, have taken in approximately 100,000 disaster victims, providing food based on headcount. There are no relief funds at all, and no resources to send them away. Sending them to the Wu River area would mean missing the planting season, and there are no seeds. Even if they are sent back, they will only end up filling ditches. If we do not quickly seek relief and maintain the current situation, I fear that the disaster victims will be completely wiped out. We earnestly request your utmost efforts to appeal and provide assistance quickly. (The rest is omitted.) (B) Telegrams from Shaanxi: (First Telegram) (The beginning is omitted.) I heard from the elderly that during the drought of the 26th year of Guangxu, there were frequent incidents of people eating people.

At first, I thought it was an exaggeration and not credible. Unexpectedly, this year, in the areas severely affected by the disaster, starving people often fill their stomachs with the buttocks and feet of dead people. It is a common sight and not considered strange. Recently, in the Zhongnan Mountains, there was a case of disaster victims eating people. There was a scrivener named Zhang, nicknamed Fatty Zhang, in Zhengxing County. Due to years of drought and famine, his business declined, so he started selling eyeglasses and went to Zhen'an County to trade. He was ambushed and killed by starving people in the Zhongnan Mountains, who divided and ate his flesh. It was extremely cruel. In recent years, countless tragedies have occurred in Shaanxi due to the disaster. (The rest is omitted.) (Second Telegram) (The beginning is omitted.) After three years of severe drought, in areas less affected by the disaster, 60-70% of the fields are barren. In areas severely affected by the disaster, all the fields are barren.

Now that spring is warm and the snow has melted, it is the time for sowing. This month, the Relief Society resolved to

issue a notice to all counties to investigate the barren land left uncultivated due to disaster-related flight, and to assign the responsibility of cultivating it to their clansmen, relatives, village chiefs, etc. Thirteen detailed rules for cultivating barren land were also established for compliance. However, most of the people in the counties have fled, and those who remain do not have the strength to buy plows, cattle, and seeds. Without substantial relief funds for assistance,

there is still no solution. We earnestly request that you find a way to provide relief. (The rest is omitted.) Looking at the above telegrams, the disaster situation in each province is urgent, and the need for relief is as urgent as a fire. We still hope that enthusiastic philanthropists from all walks of life will generously donate, regardless of the amount, and send it to the Renji Hall on Six Horse Road for receipt and collection, to be sent to the disaster areas. Saving these survivors is better than building a seven-story pagoda, as the saying goes.

Jisheng Association Discusses Allocating Cars to Transport Relief to Shaanxi

The China Jisheng Association recently received a joint telegram from Mr. Zhu Ziqiao and Mr. Zhou Jingfu, stating that the disaster situation in Qinzhong (Shaanxi) is worsening daily, with starving people lying everywhere. The spring planting season is approaching urgently, and seeds are urgently needed. However, due to road blockages and difficult transportation, there is no way to provide assistance. It has now been agreed with the Shaanxi provincial authorities to allocate a train to travel between Fengtai and Shanzhou (Shaanxi) to transport relief seeds. The telegram also requested that all charitable organizations provide assistance quickly. The association immediately telegraphed Mr. She Guisheng and Mr. Zhu Zila, the directors of the Tianjin Relief Office, to inquire about the nature of the allocated trains. If they can indeed transport grain, Mr. Zhang Xianqing from the association will bring many relief workers to Beiping (Beijing) next week to go to Shaanxi and find ways to transport seeds for relief. The disaster in Shaanxi is extremely severe. If the association can transport relief supplies by train during this urgent spring planting season, please have Mr. Zhang Xianqing go there to assess the situation and do his best to help alleviate this extraordinary disaster, even if it is only a small amount.

The Course of the Strike in Jiangqiao Town, West of Shanghai

The stores in Jiangqiao Town, west of Shanghai, went on strike the day before yesterday. It is reported that the cause was that at around 5 pm the day before yesterday, a soldier from the water patrol team stationed in the town, dressed in plain clothes and carrying a weapon, went out to investigate a case. He was spotted by a member of the security guard, who reported it to the headquarters. The headquarters immediately summoned more than 20 members, who all armed themselves and went out on patrol to prevent accidents. At the time, Li Dekui, the patrol chief of the Third Police Station of the Jiangqiao Town Branch of the First Precinct of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, was also patrolling the area with several police officers. They encountered the armed security guard and asked why they were patrolling with weapons. A slight conflict arose during the conversation. Suddenly, a gunshot was heard from the side. However, it was not clear who fired the shot. The plainclothes soldier from the water patrol team also disappeared. The police station believed that the security guard fired the shot and accused them of firing randomly, which intensified the conflict between the two sides. As a result, a member of the security guard, Mr. Qian, was taken to the town police station by the police for investigation of the gunshot. Yesterday morning, all the stores in the town went on strike because the police station did not investigate the identity of the plainclothes soldier but instead detained the security guard. Duan Wengong, the chief of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, and Wang Xixiang, the chief of the First Precinct of the Sixth District, heard the news and

immediately went to the town to inquire about the incident and summoned the town's merchants for earnest persuasion.

Therefore, all the stores resumed business as usual the day before yesterday.

Expansion of the World Moral Society

The World Moral Society at No. 90 Jing'an Temple Road established the Moral Hospital last month. Recently, the board of directors of the society decided to add a school to cultivate children's education and develop outstanding talents as the purpose. However, the society's existing premises are narrow and crowded, and the hospital is also busy with medical affairs. Therefore, it is necessary to move to a new location to expand the society's premises. It is heard that the general affairs office of the society has found suitable houses near the Aivenyi Road (Avenue Edward VII) police station. The buildings are tall and spacious, and the expansion is extraordinary. Once the chairman of the society, Mr. Xu Yabo, returns to Shanghai, the relocation will be officially carried out. In the future, the general office of the society and the hospital and school departments will all be located in the society's premises to serve the community at the same time.

Local News Two

Yesterday Morning on Qiujiang Road

Bullets Flew in a Robbery

Both Sides Fired Dozens of Shots

Two Thieves Were Wounded and Arrested

Three Police Officers Bravely Injured

Stray Bullets Wounded Two Women

At 7:15 yesterday morning, a robbery suddenly occurred at No. 1 Jingchunfang, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei.

The Second Precinct of the Fifth District and the Baoshan Road Fifth District Headquarters nearby simultaneously heard the alarm. The chiefs of each precinct led all the police officers to rush to surround and capture the thieves. Both sides fired dozens of shots, as if facing a major enemy. As a result, two thieves were wounded and captured. Three police officers were injured on the spot, and stray bullets wounded two women. Fortunately, none of the injuries were fatal. The details are recorded below:

Using a Question of Surname as a Pretense, Han Rongsheng, a local, used to work at the Asia Petroleum Company. He lived at No. 1 Jingchunfang, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, and had some savings, which attracted the attention of the robbers. At 7:15 yesterday morning, Han was out of bed, and the maid and other servants

were tidying up things in the kitchen downstairs. Suddenly, someone knocked loudly on the back door and asked loudly if Mr. Han was at home. The maid and others heard someone asking for the master and suspected it was an acquaintance, so they did not doubt it. They immediately opened the door slightly, and four people filed in. The maid shouted loudly to the master that there were guests. Han heard the sound and hurried downstairs. He looked closely at the four people and did not recognize any of them. Just as he was about to ask what was going on, the robbers had already pulled out their guns and forbade him to make a sound.

The Housewife Was Alert, Han Saw Uninvited Guests Showing Guns,

Knowing He Had Encountered Robbers, Han Pretended to Be Calm at the Time and Pretended to Ask the Robbers,

What They Wanted. The Robbers Said to Each Other, "Brothers Are in Trouble, Please Help Us." Han Agreed Generously and Led the Robbers Upstairs. The Robbers Searched the Upstairs and Took the Loot to Another Room. They Saw Many Suitcases and Ordered Han to Take the Keys to Open the Suitcases. Han Just Agreed and Turned Around

, Stepped Out of the Room, Suddenly Heard Someone Knocking Loudly on the Door. The Robbers Fled in Panic. It Turned Out That When the Robbers Entered the House, Han's Wife Had Heard the Alarm Upstairs. She Immediately Sneaked to the Drying Platform, Crossed the Neighbor's House, and Hurried to the Nearby Qiujiang Bridge Police Kiosk to Report the Crime. Then the Police Kiosk Telegraphed the Fifth District Headquarters. Chief You Heard the News and Immediately Led All the Police Officers, Fully Armed, to Surround and Capture the Thieves in Different Directions. The One Who Knocked Loudly on the Door at the Time Was the Thief Who Was Standing Guard at the Door.

Opening Fire to Resist Arrest, the Robbers Escaped from Jingchunfang, Crossed Hexingli to Qiujiang Road, and Then Turned into Yipinli. They Met Patrol Chief Gu Wentao of the Fifth District, Who Was Leading the Police to Rush to Meet Them. The Robber Immediately Opened Fire to Resist Arrest. Patrol Chief Gu Also Drew His Gun and Fired Back. Both Sides Fired More Than Ten Shots in Total. Police Officer Huan Wanhai Gave His Life to Step Forward and Hug the Robber. The Robber Continued to Fire Several Shots. Police Officer Huan Was Hit in the Right Leg by a Bullet.

At the Same Time, Patrol Chief Yuan Mingzhen, Police Officers Liu Fengtian, and Liu Desheng

Together Stepped Forward and Captured the Robber. Liu Desheng Fell and Injured His Wrist. Police Officer Yu Xiujiang's Police Uniform Was Shot Through Two Holes, Fortunately He Was Not Injured. The Original Loot Was Searched from the Robber's Side on the Spot, Including a Pair of Pearl Flowers, Thirty-Three Yuan in Silver Dollars, a Pair of Diamond Earrings, Two Gemstone Earrings, a Pair of Gold Earrings, a Gold Button, a Diamond "Fu" Character, and Five 10,000-Ruble Notes. The Robber Was Hit by a Bullet in the Right Thigh and the Lower Part of the Left Leg.

Climbing Over the Wall and Being Captured, After One Robber Was Captured, Patrol Chief Gu Ordered the Robber to Be Taken to the Headquarters First, and Then Led the Police Forward to Search. Unexpectedly, When They Reached the Thirteenth Alley of Yipinli, They Met Another Robber. The Robber Saw the Police Arriving and Immediately Drew His Gun and Fired Three Shots at Patrol Chief Gu in Succession, None of Which Hit. The Robber Fired and Fled. Patrol Chief Gu Drew His Gun and Fired Back While Chasing Closely. Chasing to the House at No. 280, Fifth Family, Twelfth Alley, the Robber Climbed Over the Wall and Escaped to the Neighboring Lianzhili. Unexpectedly, Patrol Chief Niu Kaiping Had Already Led the Police to Lie in Ambush There.

The Robber Fired Another Shot. At the Same Time, Patrol Chief Liu Dehe, Police Officers Yu Mingliang, and Zheng Xianyu All Drew Their Guns and Fired Back. The Robber Was Hit in the Right Calf by a Bullet and Collapsed to the Ground. Yu and Zheng Stepped Forward and Arrested Him. Patrol Chief Liu Took the Robber's Gun and Took Him to the Headquarters Together. Stray Bullets Injured People, Two Robbers Were Captured One After Another and Taken to the Headquarters Together. After Chief You Questioned Them One by One, The First Robber to Be Captured Confessed His Name Was Sun Jinlong, a Local, Twenty-Seven Years Old. The Second Robber to Be Captured Confessed His Name Was Lan Chunsheng, a Native of Guangdong, Twenty-Two Years Old. Both Admitted Straightforwardly to Conspiring with the Crowd to Commit Robbery. After Examining the Gunshot Wounds Suffered by the Two Robbers, Both Were Not Seriously Injured and Ordered to Be Detained Temporarily. However, When Both Sides Opened Fire, Stray Bullets Injured Two Women, One Named Wang Zhangshi, a Local, Was Hit in the Right Ankle by a Bullet, and One Named Wang Jinshi, a Native of Suzhou, Sold Zongzi (Rice Dumplings) for a Living. She Was Passing Through Yipinli and Was Hit by a Bullet in the Left Upper and Lower Legs. Chief You Ordered the Two Women to Be Sent to Guangren Hospital on Aivenyi Road First, and Police Officer Huan Wanhai Was Sent to Jisheng Hospital on Baoshan Road. The Remaining Police Officers Liu Desheng and Liu Fengtian Were Not Seriously Injured and Were Ordered to Rest. Chief You Then Reported the Detailed Situation

to the General Bureau for Verification.
