Young Lin Xueshan

Drifting at Sea in Sadness

Seeking Help from the Overseas Chinese Association

Narrating His Pain with Tears

His Father Is Doing Business in Annam

No News in Ten Months

Eating All the Pledges and Attempting Suicide

Fortunately, Someone Helped Him

On the 3rd of This Month, a Young Man Arrived at No. 478 North Sichuan Road, the Overseas Chinese Association in This Port, Stating That His Name Was Lin, Named Xueshan, Also Known as Hui, Because His Situation Was Painful, He Had Repeatedly Attempted Suicide Without Success. While Speaking, He Was in Tears, and His Situation Was Extremely Miserable. He Took Out a Letter Left to His Brother Xueqiao, Briefly Saying, "(The Beginning Is Omitted) My Will Has Been Determined, I Don't Want to Be Captured by the World Anymore, I Am Not Willing to Fight with the Disease Demon. I Am In This Poverty and Disease-Ridden Me, Only Suicide Is My Way Out, and It Is the Purification of Pain. After I Die, Everything Is Desolate, All My Luggage and Clothes Are Sold and Mortgaged Before I Die, for the Needs of Life, and Those That Remain Are Few. Brother, Do You Remember When You Caught Crickets in the Fields, Half-Hoed One, and Made a Fervent Arm to Get Out of It, and Caught It with Your Hands to See, the Hoe Was Heavy and the Insect Was Stiff, and Could Not Cry Again, the Cricket at That Time Was the Expression of My Illusory Life, (The End Is Omitted)"

After Reading It, the Person in Charge of the Association Immediately Talked to Him in Detail About Everything. According to Him, His Father's Hometown Was Qiongzhou, and He Had Been Doing Business in French Annam for Many Years. He Was Born in Annam. In the 17th Year of the Republic of China, He Came to Shanghai to Study at the China-France Specialized School on Lafayette Road. Later, He Gave Up His Studies Due to Illness. His Living Expenses Were Always Sent by His Father, About 1,000 Yuan a Year. However, in the Last Ten Months, He Repeatedly Sent Letters Urging Him, But There Was No Reply, and His Life and Death Were Unknown, Which Was Very Anxious. Within These Ten Months, His Life Was Embarrassing, and No One Helped Him. He Had Short Ideas and Repeatedly Attempted Suicide Without Success. According to This Association, in Addition to Finding Ways to Maintain His Accommodation and Food for a Day or Two, He Was Also Introduced to the Shanghai Career Guidance Center to Give Him Guidance. Ho Yun Seeks Opportunities to Find Jobs on His Behalf, But Before He Gets a Real Job, How Should His Life Be Maintained, It Is Difficult to Ignore It, Because of Browsing the Shanghai Special City Social Bureau, Which Is Most Concerned About Suicide Cases, and Often Tries Its Best to Provide Relief, So He Asked the Shanghai Career Guidance Center to Introduce Lin Jun to Visit the Social Bureau Staff with a Letter, and Asked for Assistance. Now the Association and the Guidance Center Have Received a Reply from the Fourth Section of the Social Bureau, Briefly Saying That, in Addition to Instructing the Student to Trouble Your Association to Investigate the Relatives or Friends of the Student in Annam to Find Ways to Notify,

Has Been Sent to the Shanghai New Puyutang for Temporary Custody,

The Car Injured

Small Laborer Carried to Court

Circumstances of Chen Shu's Accident

Compensation Demanded for Deceased

Judge Pronounces Verdict in Court

Total Fine of Six Hundred Yuan

At approximately 5:30 PM on the 6th of this month, two laborers from Jiangbei, Xie Zhitang and Zhu Yulin, were jointly carrying a large log, about thirty feet long and six feet wide. As they were walking on Yuyuan Road in Shanghai's western district, just as they were turning into a lane, a Suzhou native, Lu Quan'gen, driving car number 4898, sped towards them. The driver was unable to avoid them in time, causing the car to collide with the log. The massive log fell, injuring both Xie and Zhu. Upon investigation, the patrolmen arrested the car driver Lu Quan'gen and detained him at the Jing'an Temple police station. The two injured men were taken to Dehe Hospital.

Xie's injuries were so severe that he died the next day despite medical treatment. Zhu's injuries were minor, and he remained in the hospital for treatment. The hospital notified the police station, which sent officers to transport Xie's body to the coroner's office for examination. Yesterday morning, the police station escorted Lu Quan'gen to the Special District Court. Representatives of the deceased's family hired a lawyer to appear in court, stating that the deceased, Xie Zhitang, worked in a factory, earning a monthly salary of approximately thirty yuan, upon which his entire family depended for their livelihood. Now, he has tragically been crushed to death.

Therefore, they filed a civil suit, demanding compensation for funeral expenses, calculated over a ten-year period, totaling three thousand yuan. As for Zhu Yulin, whose injuries were minor,

they also requested reimbursement for medical expenses amounting to fifty yuan. Subsequently, Mr. Ru Bao from the police station provided an account of the incident. Zhu Yulin, the injured party, was carried into court and testified that he and the deceased were carrying a large log together and were turning into the lane when the defendant drove

at high speed, knocking him down. However, he did not see the defendant's car beforehand, nor did he hear a horn. The accident was indeed caused by the defendant's excessive speed. When questioned, the defendant claimed that he was driving through Yuyuan Road at a moderate speed.

The plaintiffs were carrying the log from the opposite direction. As his car approached, the plaintiffs suddenly turned the log horizontally, intending to carry it into the lane. He immediately tried to swerve to avoid them, but the log was exceptionally long,

blocking the entire road. Even though he steered his car to the side of the road, there was no way to avoid the accident. Subsequently, Mr. Ru, the lawyer from the police station, and Mr. Jiang Yiping, the lawyer hired by the defendant, engaged in a debate, arguing extensively about

the circumstances and the issue of negligence. Judge Wu Tingqi reviewed the testimonies, declared the debate closed, and pronounced the verdict in court. The main text read: "The defendant, Lu Quan'gen, is found guilty of causing death through negligence and is fined five hundred yuan. For the crime of causing injury through negligence,

he is fined two hundred yuan. The total fine is six hundred yuan. For each two days of detention before the judgment is finalized, one yuan will be deducted from the fine. If the fine is not paid through enforcement, imprisonment will be substituted at a rate of two yuan per day. The attached civil suit will be transferred to the civil court for handling."

Special District Court

Opening of Foreign Cases

First Trial Yesterday

Brought by British and American Firms

Better Order Than Before

New Court Displays Vigor

With the establishment of the Shanghai Special District Court, the system of consular jury trials that had existed for decades has come to an end. In the future, the court will hear criminal and civil cases brought by foreign nationals against Chinese citizens without the need for juries. Although the Japanese initially objected to the abolition of juries,

they have recently complied. President Yang of the court believes that the number of cases accepted from merchants of various countries, both old and new, is very high, and trials should be conducted in succession to avoid backlog. Each civil court judge has set trial dates and instructed officials to notify the parties concerned separately to report on schedule and await trial.

Yesterday morning marked the first day of the opening of foreign cases after the establishment of the court. Judge Ying Shi, Head of the Civil Court, Judge Zhou Daren,

and Judges Pang Shurong and Luo Chongtai of the Summary Court each opened the seventh, eighth, ninth, and tenth courts respectively, to hear several cases brought by British and American firms to recover loans. Consuls from Britain, America, and other countries all complied with the newly signed agreements and abandoned jury trials. The lawyers for the plaintiffs in each case were all foreign nationals, who brought interpreters to the court to translate. The presiding judge experienced no communication barrier. The order was better than when there were consular juries in the past. Because the judge alone conducted the interrogation, without interference from others, no unnecessary incidents occurred. And since there were no disputes, the conclusion of a case was not delayed. Therefore, the abolition of the consular jury system,

while subjectively reclaiming our country's legal rights, objectively benefits foreign nationals living in Shanghai.

The Wusong Chamber of Commerce requests improvements to the

Steam Train Facilities on the Songhu Road

Since the Shanghai branch road was converted to steam train traffic, passengers have praised the convenience of travel and the accuracy of the timetable. It is now known that Zheng Shushan, Chairman of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, believes that there are several aspects of the facilities of the train that must be improved. (1)

When the train is running, many sparks fly out of the chimney. When the wind carries them far, they can land on the houses along the road, easily causing disaster. Furthermore, the houses are densely packed along the road, and the grass houses near the Zhanghuabang Railway were recently burned down when sparks from the steam train flew out. It is essential to find a way to improve this situation to prevent further danger. (2) Adding a Gaojingmiao station between Jiangwan and Zhanghuabang would be

very convenient for passengers in the Yinhang area. However, the area is quite desolate, with few pedestrians, and there is concern that it may be targeted by bandits, especially at night. The railway bureau should deploy armed police to patrol the station regularly to protect passenger safety. Yesterday, the Wusong Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to Director Liu of the railway bureau, requesting improvements to achieve perfection.

Mayor Zhang

Visits the Shanghai Waterworks Company

Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, Mr. Bi Yaxun, Chief Engineer and Manager of the Shanghai Waterworks Company, invited Mayor Zhang and his wife to visit the Yangshupu Waterworks Plant. They were accompanied by Mr. Huang Boqiao, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, and Mr. Zou Enyong, Chief Technician. They toured the various water pools, pump rooms, boiler rooms, and laboratories. Mr. Bi Yaxun, along with Mr. Li Tu, Chairman of the company, and Mr. Walter, the secretary, led the tour and provided warm hospitality. Mayor Zhang and others felt that the plant's equipment was complete, the layout was organized, and the scale was quite grand, which they greatly praised. Mr. Bi Yaxun originally intended to invite the Mayor to visit the workers' residences and schools in the northern part of the plant, but Mayor Zhang had official duties and could not stay long, so he took his leave.

Headquarters

Robber Shi Jinquan Executed Yesterday

The case of the robbery and murder of Yuan A'si, a resident of No. 2 Yuqing Lane, Yangjiadu South End, Pudong, on January 23 of this year, was solved by the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, who arrested five suspects, Chen A'er, Shi Jinquan, Hao Zhenqi, Liu Hongru, and Xu Zhengwen, in the Dapuqiao area of the French Concession. They were submitted to the Military Law Department of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. The interrogation has concluded. Shi Jinquan was taken out yesterday afternoon, handed over to the Public Security Bureau, and officers were ordered to escort him to Yangjiadu, Pudong, to be executed by firing squad on the spot. The prisoner shouted "Injustice" all the way. Upon reaching the destination, he was forcibly led down by the police, and a total of three shots were fired, two hitting the head,

and one hitting the back, killing him. The body was collected by the local保甲 and temporarily placed in the empty lot of Yu Family Temple, awaiting identification by relatives. During the execution, onlookers surrounded the area like a wall. Detective Zhang Yong and others from the Third District Police Station and the Battalion Commander of the First Division were present to oversee the proceedings. The Public Notice No. 50 (法字) of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters is recorded below as a notification: The Municipal Public Security Bureau presented the case of robbers Shi Jinquan and others to the Department. After interrogation, except for Hao Zhenqi and Liu Hongru, who were each sentenced to an indefinite term of imprisonment according to law and sent to prison for execution, Shi Jinquan was sentenced to death for his actions of holding weapons, gang robbery, and intentional homicide. In addition to presenting the prisoner Shi Jinquan for verification of his

identity and handing him over to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to be tied up and taken to the execution ground for execution by firing squad,

this notice is issued to inform the public.

The executed prisoner Shi Jinquan, 27 years old, from Zhenjiang, Republic of China, April 9, 19th year, Commander Xiong Shihui.

Ningbo Barge Damaged by British Ship

The Guild is Negotiating

According to sources from the Siming Transport Barge and Coal Ship Guild, the Ningbo boat owner Zhong Xiaoqing's barge, captained by Chen Xiaowu, was carrying stones when, at 7:05 AM on April 2nd, it was traveling from Puxi to Pudong. As it approached the Lujiazui Water Police Station, the British firm Bảo Ho Company's Sunland vessel, being towed by a tug, was also sailing in the area. At this time, the tug suddenly gave way, causing the ship's bow to lose control and proceed directly toward the Water Police Station. The barge had no room to maneuver in the

tight space, and its front (left side) was struck by the massive vessel, causing significant damage. However, another vessel, Uarilc,

was observing behind the barge and noted minor damage. Zhong Xiaoqing reported to the Siming Transport Barge and Coal Ship Guild, requesting assistance. Bao Ho Company requested Paulsen, David & Co., surveyors, to conduct an assessment and jointly discuss compensation methods with representatives from the guild. However, the company only acknowledged that the damage to the rear of the barge was caused by them, leading to a temporary impasse. It is confirmed that the nc!j!e merchant vessel was small and was indeed observing behind the barge, and the damaged boat is still present, making it easy to understand the events. However, the circumstances at the time can be proven by other vessels. It is reported that this matter is still under negotiation.

Municipal Government

Prohibiting the Dumping of Trash in the Huangpu River

The Municipal Government recently discovered garbage barges arbitrarily dumping waste in the Huangpu River, which it considers detrimental to both hygiene and the river channel. It has specifically ordered the Sanitation and Public Safety Bureaus to strictly prohibit this and to implement the various measures for escorting garbage ships adopted by the bureau's meetings.

Assassin of Opera Singer Arrested

Xiao Yuehua, a Yangzhou opera singer at the Qingsheng Theater on Route Aoulléga, was assassinated in early December of the previous year, as previously reported. Although the military and police authorities have continued to investigate the case, the assassin has remained at large. However, on the night before last, detectives Xin Jingsheng, Chen Guangxiang, Xu Haishan, and Lu Tingshu from the Fifth District of Zhabei received a tip that the assassin, Zhang Yucai (also known as Dalianzi),

was watching a play at the Dingxin Stage near Hujia Wood Bridge. The detectives, carrying concealed weapons, proceeded to the location and arrested Zhang on the spot. He was taken to the station and questioned, but Zhang refused to confess. Yesterday, a document was prepared and submitted to the Judicial Section for punishment.

Tragic Death from Falling Down Stairs

Xu Yongjin, a Suzhou native, 33 years old, residing at No. 58 Songhe Lane, Route Vilmont, French Concession, worked as a tea server in a theater.

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, after getting up and washing his face, he went upstairs and, for unknown reasons, suddenly fell on the stairs and rolled down, cracking his skull and dying instantly. His family reported to the police, who ordered detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang Verification Office to await an autopsy.

Maid Dies of Poisoning

Master Charged with Neglect

Delayed Sending to Hospital for Five Hours

Anhui elder Wang Xunzu, represented by a lawyer, filed a lawsuit at the French Court, claiming that his daughter-in-law, Wang Wangshi, was working as a maid at Wang Senchang's lumber yard when she was abused by Wang and his wife, leading to her death by poisoning. The case was heard again yesterday. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that there was a five-hour delay between the time the deceased took the poison and when the police were notified and she was sent to the hospital. The deceased was suffering from an acute condition. How could there be such a delay? This shows that the defendant had malicious intentions.

Moreover, after her death, the defendant did not contribute to her funeral expenses, which were covered by a charitable organization. The defendant showed no compassion. Such cruelty is evident. He requested an investigation and compensation for bereavement, etc. When questioned, Wang Senchang stated that the deceased had been working as a maid in his business for just seventeen days.

She often cried privately. When asked, she revealed that her husband had been sentenced to seven years in the Caohejing Prison for committing a crime. Her suicide was likely due to her resentment of her fate. However, he had treated her very well and there was no abuse. Please investigate. Judge Zhu Cheng stated that the case was important.

Further investigation would be conducted. A new date would be set for review.

Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities

Handling Various Registration Statistics

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities handles various registrations. The work is very heavy. In terms of water supply, there are five types of registration: water pipe merchants, water pipe industry owners, self-owned water supply equipment, well drilling companies, and well drilling projects. In terms of electricity, there are four types of registration: electrical supply stores, electrical contractors, user's in-house wiring electricians, and wiring apprentices. In terms of land transportation, there are car companies,

gas stations, car drivers, and various vehicles. In terms of water transportation, there are Wusong River ferries and cargo boats. The registration deadlines have passed successively. After continuous progress and retreat, the statistical results as of the end of March 19, compared to the previous year, showed an increase. The totals for each registration are listed below: (A) Water Supply: (1) 34 water pipe merchants, (2) 212 water pipe workers, (3) 356 property owners with self-owned water supply equipment, (4) 14 well drilling companies, (5)

25 well drilling projects; (B) Electricity: (1) 99 electrical supply stores, (2) 5 electrical contractors, (3) 257 wiring electricians, (4) 206 wiring apprentices; (C) Land Transportation: (1) 52 car companies, (2) 37 gas stations,

(3) 7,649 car drivers, (4) 57,880 vehicles of all types, including 4,840 cars;

(D) Water Transportation: (1) 14 Wusong River ferries, (2) 10,210 cargo ships, (3) 1,283 rowing boats.

Reactionary Element Chen Moke Apprehended

Hua Guo, a Chinese detective from the General Police Station, lived at No. 475 Mctaggart Hurst Road, Xuhui. Recently, Chen Moke (also known as Chen Zhonghao and Chen Bi Kuang), from Anhui, moved into the pavilion room of his house. The detective noticed that he was behaving suspiciously. After secretly investigating for several days, he learned that Chen was a reactionary element. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 1:10 PM, he reported to Detective Evans, the West Detective Chief of the Political Department, and with the assistance of Detective Gu Weiqing and the local Gordon Road Police Station detective Gao Zhen, went to the address and arrested Chen. Reactionary leaflets and books, as well as shredded leaflets, were found under the bed and on the desk. All were taken to the police station. Yesterday afternoon, he was transferred to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court.

Judge Song Yuan, along with Judges Du Fuyue and Ye Zaichou, and Chief Prosecutor Wang Zhennan, heard the case. Mr. Ru Bao, the police lawyer, stated the case and presented the various reactionary publications seized. Detectives Ding and Gao then reported the circumstances of the arrest. Chen Moke claimed that he had previously worked as a secretary in the Anhui Provincial Party Department. These publications were brought by Mr. Li Junda on the evening of the 6th of this month to be temporarily stored.

There were two packages, large and small. He said he would pick them up the next day, but Mr. Li disappeared without a trace. He did not know that they contained reactionary documents. Judge Song reviewed the testimony and ordered Chen to be detained for another hearing on the morning of the 12th of this month.

Mother's Brother's Heinous Act

Trying to Sell Niece as a Prostitute

Dai A'ren, a woman from Jiaxing, 18 years old, lost both parents at a young age and lived with her stepmother. Last month, she was brought to Shanghai by her maternal uncle, Fang Zhicai, under the pretext of helping with household chores. He asked Yang Desheng to introduce her to Cao Wangshi, a woman from Yangzhou in the French Concession, as a prostitute. The asking price was 240 yuan, but the transaction had not been completed. Detective Ding Wensheng of the French Concession Police learned of this and arrested all the people involved. Yesterday, they were sent to the French Court for investigation. The police chief reported the details, stating that the defendant was found to be enticing a virtuous woman into prostitution, which constituted crimes under Articles 247, 257, and

358 of the criminal law. He requested a severe investigation. When questioned, Fang Zhicai,

admitted that he had indeed brought his niece to Shanghai to sell her into prostitution. Yang Desheng confessed that he knew Fang Zhicai and that Fang had asked him to introduce his niece to Mrs. Wang as a prostitute. When the woman, Dai A'ren, was questioned, she stated that her parents had died early and she was living with her stepmother in her hometown. This time, her uncle brought her to Shanghai, falsely claiming that he was taking her to Mrs. Wang's house to help with household chores, but he forced her to become a prostitute. However, she did not want to pursue this low profession. She requested to be released. Cao Wangshi stated that Dai A'ren had been brought by Yang Desheng for prostitution. The Chinese and foreign judges sentenced Fang Zhicai to six months in the Western Jail, and Yang Desheng and Cao Wangshi to four months each as a warning. Dai was sent to an institution to find a suitable match.

Passenger Dies Without Speaking

Unknown Person

Also Unknown Surname

At approximately 7:30 AM on the 29th of last month, the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway's Shanghai-added Police Department at the South Station found a passenger, over forty years old, in a third-class carriage of train number 7 from Hangzhou. He was wearing a blue satin cotton robe, a black satin mandarin jacket, and a black satin cap, lying on the train and unable to speak. He appeared to be suffering from aphasia or madness. Deputy Section Chief Duan Jianhuan of the Police Department, together with the station manager, sent officers to help the passenger to the station's waiting room.

Upon inspection, he had 20 yuan in silver coins, 6 jiao in small coins, 25 copper coins, a pair of glasses, two handkerchiefs, and three keys, but no business card. The Police Department temporarily took custody of these items. Officers were sent to the Shanghai Hospital for treatment. He died yesterday afternoon due to his illness. Until his death, he was unable to speak, so his name and address are unknown. The Police Department has reported to the local court and scheduled an autopsy for today (the 10th). Photographs will be taken for identification purposes.

In the Huangpu River

Kidnapping-Style Robbery

Pier boat owner Wu Haisheng ordered helmsman Fan Xiaohai the other day, to direct the boat crew, to successively row to the Taikoo Company pier, and the Huashun pier, Mute pier, Fair pier, to load a roll of Ning silks from Xin Shenchang Yishun Heng Yongfengli and other three customs brokers,

a roll of green thick tribute wool, a roll of black thick tribute wool, a piece of waterfall city cloth (50 bolts in total), four pieces of Da Xi silk, a piece of 克羅紗, and a piece of satinet. After loading was completed at about 8 PM, they rowed from Hongkou to the Longmao pier in Pudong to unload. When passing the surface of the river near the mouth of the Suzhou River, a double-oared boat suddenly approached the boat. Docking alongside, eight robbers with handguns jumped over the boat, first tying up the crew, including the helmsman, and throwing them into the rear hold. Then, they completely transferred the cargo to the rowing boat and escaped without a trace. After the cargo boat was robbed, the thieves rowed it to a berth near the Xin Zha Jiangyuan Alley in the Suzhou River, and the helmsman and crew were confined in the hold, unable to escape. Until 4 AM yesterday morning, the three customs brokers found that the boat and cargo were missing and sent people to search in all directions, and finally found the boat at the location and released the helmsman, etc., and found that all the cargo had been stolen,

resulting in great loss. They reported to the respective firms, and in the morning, they declared the losses and sent people to report to the Water Police Station for investigation. The police chief, upon receiving the report,

said that the robbers dared to commit robbery with weapons on the river surface, which seriously hindered water transportation. He specifically ordered all detectives and police to step up their pursuit,

and to arrest all the criminals and bring them to justice to quell the banditry.

Kiln Collapse Crushes Boatman

Ge Xiaofenzi, a Bloody Mess, Was Usually Engaged in Transporting Goods by Boat on the Suzhou River at Zhoujia Bridge, Xuhui. Ge Zhouyu, 50 years old, from Yancheng, had only one son named Ge Xiaofenzi, who was fifteen years old and cared for the boat with his father. He was very diligent and thrifty and was very loved by his father. At about 7 PM the day before yesterday, Ge's boat was carrying a load of 三合土 and sailed to the lime kiln area of Xiaoshadu to dock. Ge and his son went ashore to the kiln set up by Wu Zhao to load. However, the kiln had been damaged for many years. Not long after loading began, there was a sudden "bang" sound, and the high walls of the kiln collapsed. Ge's son, Xiaofenzi, was unable to escape and was buried in the dirt. Ge and others in the kiln immediately tried to rescue him, but he had suffered severe injuries, was a bloody mess, and had already died. Ge Zhouyu reported this to the local Sixth District Police Station. The police were immediately dispatched to the scene and summoned the kiln owner Wu Zhao and manager Wang Shaoqing for questioning. After separate interrogations by District Chief Duan, according to the plaintiff Ge Zhouyu, he was 50 years old, from Yancheng, and he requested an allowance because he only had one son. Wu Zhao claimed that he was 16 years old, from Yancheng, and that the kiln was set up by his older brother. Wang Shaoqing stated that he was 40 years old, from Ningbo,

and had been working as the manager of the kiln. After receiving the statements, District Chief Duan immediately ordered the police to summon Wu Zhao's brother. Today, a document will be prepared and submitted to the local court for investigation. Subsequently, the local保甲 Zhang Xietang reported to the local court, requesting to send personnel to verify the situation. Later, at about 4 PM, the court appointed Prosecutor Li Gongchen and Secretary Deng Zhenwei to bring with them to verify the scene. It was found that the boy had been crushed to death before his death due to severe injuries. He ordered the father of the corpse, Ge Zhouyu, to prepare a coffin first and then continue the investigation.

Disappearance of Miss Tang

Believed to Be Abducted by Xu Yangchun

Tang Libang, 48 years old, from Yancheng, residing at No. 109 Xitan, Xiaoshadu, Xuhui, runs a private school at home, teaching children for a living. He has a daughter named Guannan, eighteen years old, who is unmarried. She works at the Robison Road Xihe Yarn Factory, going in the morning and returning in the evening. Unexpectedly, on the 28th of last month, his daughter suddenly disappeared. Tang searched everywhere, but without success. Until recently, a fellow villager, Ge Xinglin, reported to Tang that earlier this month, he had seen Xu Yangchun from Baoying walking on the road with the daughter. Because he knew that Xu worked in the same factory as the daughter, he did not suspect anything else. Now that the daughter has been abducted and is missing, it must be that Xu has abducted her. Therefore, Tang, accompanied by witness Ge Xinglin, went to the Xiaoshadu Lime Kiln the other day and arrested Xu Yangchun, reporting to the Sixth District Police Station. After separate interrogations by District Chief Duan, because the case involved abduction, the case was submitted to the court for investigation yesterday.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River Basin, the coastal areas of Shanghai, and the area south of Ma'anshan are cloudy with showers, or thunderstorms. There is a cyclone in the Shanghai area and north of the East China Sea, due to a low pressure moving east or northeast. The Shandong coast is cloudy,

and the northeast wind is strengthening. Yesterday, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 65.8 degrees and the lowest was 52.3 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 72.8 degrees and the lowest was 44.0 degrees.

Free Talk

Lament for the Fallen Soldiers

— Zheng Zhian

Mourning the Soldiers Who Died Defending the Northeast Border

Smoke and dust rise on the Heilong River. Urgent dispatches travel thousands of miles in a single night. There is no day to settle the Central Plains. Someone borrows chopsticks to plan the northern frontier. The northern frontier is isolated, guarded by soldiers. For a time, passion stirred the winds and clouds. How could there be any hardship in being a soldier?

On the borderlands, everlasting are the merits of resisting the invaders. Deep trenches and high ramparts were arranged early. In their eyes, they only hated that there were too few who shared their hatred. The brave troops were first marked at Luoyan City; news of victories has already spread to Lianyun Fortress. A separate force comes on the water. The sound of the river is even more mournful than the sound of the horns. Still relying on a torch within the gourd, not letting the iron locks of the Yellow River be opened. The powerful enemy will not look with ordinary eyes.

Charging like boars, fleeing like wolves, they come and go. Startled by shadows, the white geese fly. Who remembers the Yellow Dragon garrisons, wounded? The invaders come again on the Yiluo River. How to wait when strength is exhausted and aid is cut off? Who knows that after measuring sand in the middle of the night, they still sing the ancient "Chil Le Song"? It is a man's duty to give up life for righteousness. Holding their beards, they will not betray their lifelong ambitions.

How desolate, after death, is the light yellow uniform. How generous, within their hearts, are the dried ink words. I sigh that there was a Han in the army (referring to Brigade Commander Han Guangdi), leaving only old fortifications for people to see. Who knows where Xian Zhen is now? Only Wang Lin's blood remains, not yet cold. In Liaoyang in the third month, the clouds are still frozen. Who, after the pain subsides, still thinks of the pain?

The cold moon summons the souls of the patriots. The mournful wind blows apart the dreams of women in their spring boudoirs. They sacrificed their seven-foot bodies for the country. No need to resent the crows and kites that peck at their flesh. Let us take a spoonful of yellow-sealed wine and toast from afar to the ancient green-bricked tomb.

The results of each event have been detailed in various newspapers. Even the anecdotes of the Games have been published as much as possible in various newspapers. However, the food consumption of the Games seems to have not yet been mentioned. This is also quite interesting. The results of the survey from the Games' kitchen are recorded below.

During the first, second, and third days after the opening of the Games, a total of 300 tables were needed per meal for athletes and referees, and about 100 tables for other staff. Continued Biography of Physical Educationist Wei Xudong

— Xu Fan

The facts about the physical educationist Wei Xudong mentioned in the previous article are very accurate.

However, I studied in Wumen in my early years, and I listened to Mr. Wei's teachings for several years. Therefore, I know his history in more detail. I will continue to record one or two things as a commemoration.

Mr. Wei's given name was Tinghui, and Xudong was his courtesy name. Wei Guangshou, the Viceroy of Liangjiang in the Manchu Qing Dynasty, was his ancestor. When the new army was reorganized,

a preparatory military academy was established in Baixia. Mr. Wei was selected from the ranks to enter.

After completing his studies, he was tested. He was the best in practical skills. He was at the bottom in academic subjects. In the end, because of his excellent technical skills, he was still ranked among the best. Mr. Wei was magnanimous and did not shy away from mentioning his academic weakness. Later, Lu Chunjian, the Governor of Jiangsu, appointed Mr. Wei to a physical education position at a higher school. Mr. Wei immediately equipped the school with exercise equipment such as horizontal bars, wooden horses, aerial ladders, and platforms. In addition to the daily

Matchmaking Bamboo

— Ji Jin

Matchmaking bamboo, commonly known as "Double Union Bamboo," is produced in Liaoxi Estuary, northeast of Guangzhou. Two plants are integrated as one.

The branches and leaves intertwine. The appearance is not very different. Saw it open and you can see two holes, shaped like the character "吕". According to the locals, in the past, a young boy and girl (their era and surnames are not verifiable) were playing by the stream. Each held one end of a green bamboo stick and threw it into the middle of the stream, declaring that if the two bamboo sticks joined together, they would become husband and wife. Looking at it, it was indeed so.

They returned to tell their parents, and eventually, they were engaged. Enthusiasts transplanted this bamboo to the area, and it grew luxuriantly. Therefore, the pool was named "Betrothal Pool." The pool is in Liaoxi Estuary, where matchmaking bamboo groves grow on both sides, full of charm. Now, my friend Mr. Li returned from Guangdong and gave me a branch. It is about five feet long. All the leaves have fallen off, but the base still has stems and whiskers. He said that it can be revived. I will plant it in the garden and cover it with soil. But I don't know if it has a chance to live.

Teaching military drills, he patiently taught apparatus exercises. He often practiced on the parade ground when the sun was setting, allowing people to watch. He was capable of feats such as lifting a tripod, spinning on the iron bar, and executing cartwheels with the energy of dozens of revolutions. He was light, agile, and as fast as an electric wheel, surprising everyone who saw him.

And Mr. Wei's great reputation spread far and wide.

At that time, there were few schools in Wumen. The education authorities did not supervise sports meets or recreational events. However, in order to promote the spirit of martial arts, Mr. Wei first organized a sports meet at the higher school. Soon, alumni from Soochow University and the Second Normal School responded and participated. Mr. Wei often took the opportunity at gatherings to promote the benefits of physical education for the human body. Because of Mr. Wei, the weak customs of Wuxia began to compete in advocating martial arts. Later, the Suzhou Chamber of Commerce was established, and Mr. Wei was also hired as the commander. At that time, Mr. Wei was also teaching at Soochow University, devoting all his energy to guiding physical education. In the last years of the Guangxu era, he was also hired as a coach by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, dividing his time between Suzhou and Shanghai, teaching on a rotating schedule. From then on, he held the reins of physical education for students and businessmen in Suzhou and Shanghai.

Mr. Wei liked to ride horses and bicycles. When riding a horse at full speed, he would deliberately drop his hat on the ground and be able to whip his horse back, dash past the original spot, suddenly jump down, pick up the hat, and leave. When riding a bicycle, he would stand on one foot on the bike's handlebar while the wheels were spinning rapidly, or he would perform a feat of lifting a tripod, or he would jump off the ground and let the bike continue to move forward. Mr. Wei would chase after the bike, jump back on, and sit upright, pedaling. His speed was amazing. At that time, a certain coach of the 45th Regiment was also known for his skills. With the introduction of Liu Jieyu, the secretary of the regiment (that is, a farmer from Tiantai Mountain), he once competed with Mr. Wei after a sports meet. In the end, Mr. Wei won the championship. Mr. Wei was humble and approachable and also enjoyed having fun with others.

It is a pity that he has now passed away and we will never see Mr. Wei's skills again.

Record of Cherry Blossom Viewing at Jinchang

— Xiaohou

As a reporter, I traveled to Suzhou for the reorganization of the Jiangsu Provincial Newspaper Association. After arriving in Suzhou, I was accompanied by Qiu Kun, the chief editor of the Suzhou Ming Pao, and reporter Chen Shipei to visit Tianping and Tiger Hill, as well as Dengwei to see the plum blossoms. After the trip, my old friend Wu Xinshan from Jinling came to visit. I talked to him about my trip to the East last autumn and regretted not being able to see the cherry blossoms on the three islands due to the timing. He said that in Qingyang, outside the Panmen Gate of Suzhou, the cherry blossoms were now in full bloom, and what could not be obtained on the three islands of Fusang could be obtained domestically. At that time, I was packing my bags, planning to take the 5:00 PM express train to Zhenjiang. It was less than three hours before the train departed. Mr. Wu strongly urged me to go.

So we rode in a car together. With a whip and the setting sun, the sound of hooves pattered. We arrived at our destination in about ten minutes. Looking closely, the cherry blossoms were arranged in rows.

The petals resembled peaches and plums, but the color was pink, as bright as brocade, winding for about a mile. At the entrance, there was a sign that said "Stop Vehicles and Horses". Visitors must get out of their cars and walk from here. However, Japanese policemen in uniforms patrolled the cherry blossom ranks on bicycles.

Women in wooden sandals strolled around, leisurely and content. According to Mr. Wu, who traveled with me, this place has always been a Japanese concession. The Japanese consulate resides here, with an attached Japanese police station, which is beyond the control of our Chinese governance. Recently, I heard that because the market is deserted, there is talk of our country taking it back, imitating the British concession in Zhenjiang. I still remember last spring, when I traveled with my colleague Chen Shaojun from Jinling New Village, serving my mother on a trip to West Lake. On the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road, we agreed that this spring, we would go to Japan early for the Far Eastern Games to see the cherry blossoms. There was also a couplet that read: The railway dragon snakes travel across the continent,

Lovers from New Village travel together. Looking at the green trees and green mountains from afar, all are collected in the eyes of the spring clouds. Now, Shaojun is stimulated by the environment and stays at home with his mother, retreating and not asking about worldly affairs. I, as a reporter, am still wandering around, with no place to settle down. Recalling past events, I cannot help but feel the difference between now and then.

Red Rug

Grand Rehearsal of the Bayi Yaji Society

— Ruo

The Bayi Yaji Society was established on February 23rd, only a little more than a month ago. Most of the members of the society are experienced amateur opera performers, so with just a brief explanation from the teachers and a short period of practice, they can perform on stage. On the 6th of this month, the society specially rehearsed and sang at the Ningbo Tongxiang Association for one day and night as a memento. I will record what I saw during the day. The performance began at around 1 p.m. Chen Boyong performed two excerpts in a row, one being "Golden Stage," playing Tian Dan, and the other being "Chain Links," playing Huang Tianba. This man has sufficient capital and a broad voice. He handled the performance with ease. The upside-down board of "Golden Stage," singing the "ga" tune, was especially energetic. "Scolding the Palace" was not performed due to time constraints. Instead, they performed "Catching and Releasing Cao," which was quite natural in both singing and acting. As the saying goes, "It takes a long road to know a horse's strength." Because I was backstage tuning someone's voice, I didn't get to hear it. Then, "Yellow Crane Tower" took the stage, with Chen Boyong playing Liu Bei and Wei Xinsun playing Zhou Yu, each excelling in their own way. Mr. Wei sang a section of "Southern Bangzi," which was melodious and pleasant to the ear. Next was Wang Guansan and Wei Fusun's performance of "Farewell at the Kiln." Mr. Wang played Pinggui, with a moderate build. His posture in the "Qi Ba" was both neat and lively. At the beginning, he said, "Helping and protecting the Tang king establish great merit," which won him a full house of applause. Mr. Wei's Wang Baochuan had a beautiful appearance. Her acting strictly adhered to the rules. After the opening introduction, she sang a large passage of "Zheng Erhuang," with accurate notes and round tones, showing her skill. As for the performance of the emotions of a couple parting, it was also just right.

Whenever I watch this play being performed, it often makes my hair stand on end. The performances of these two gentlemen did not have these shortcomings, which shows the depth of their research. Mr. Wei asked me to play the role of the stringed instrument in this play. I reluctantly took on the role. Fortunately, there were no major mistakes. Following this was Zhang Yisheng's "Disturbing the Government Office." Mr. Zhang is an old amateur opera singer from Beiping, singing in the style of Uncle Yan. He is full of flavor. His posture in "Asking the Woodcutter" is skilled and refined, truly like an expert. It is not easy. The final act was Zhao Zuichiu's "Yutangchun." Mr. Zhao's appearance was exceptionally charming. In the "Xipi Slow Board" and "Original Board," almost every tune he sang was in the style of Cheng, and every sentence was new. The accompaniment of the Li brothers was also excellent. The role of Wang Gongzi in this play was played by the famous amateur opera singer Mr. Nie Shaoxuan, which added a lot of color to the performance.

A New Way to See the Peach Blossoms at Longhua

— Yan Qian

The peach blossoms at Longhua, like ten thousand pieces of red clouds, stretch for miles. It is truly a great sight on the sea. However, in the past, we only knew to invite friends to drive or walk there together, never knowing that there were other ways to appreciate them besides walking through the woods.

The author recently took the Xinminxin ship from Desheng Port to Shanghai. When passing Longhua Mouth, I saw patches of red clouds from afar, as if being pushed by the wind, or as if thousands of women in red were dancing in groups. The impression was better than walking through the woods by far.

After returning, I talked to my friends about it. They all said that this fact was as pleasing as discovering a new continent. So we discussed and planned new ways to see the flowers, and we came up with three ideas.

The first to speak was Mr. Shen, who said that it would be best to drive a motorboat, sail along the shallow shore, and go back and forth slowly for a deeper appreciation. We could prepare wine, dried meat, and fine tea on the boat to accompany the tour.

Next, Mr. Shi said that it would be best to have those who have learned to swim and are good at paddling row small boats and tour, so that not only could the peach blossoms on land be appreciated to the fullest, but also the beautiful reflections on the water could be played with at will. Finally, Mr. Liang said that it would be best to sit on a Western-style small sailboat and let it drift on the gentle breeze, so that the reflection of the sail in the red flowers would be greatly appreciated.

The author said that the ideas of the three gentlemen were actually three in one. It could be generally called "A New Way to See the Peach Blossoms at Longhua". I will record it as a free talk and make it public to everyone. The three gentlemen agreed that it was good, so I wrote it down.

Humorous Common Sense

— Ye Limin

If there is a hole in the heel of a black sock,

and a piece of flesh is exposed when you put on your shoes, wouldn't it be very unsightly? You can use ink to paint the flesh,

so that people won't be able to see it anymore.

Do not discard a broken umbrella. You can remove the umbrella ribs and use it as a walking stick.

If a sock is torn, cut off the torn part. It can be used as a sleeve or a foot cover.

If you can't afford to buy a clock, just buy a chicken. It can tell the time, and you can also taste its meat. Wouldn't it be killing two birds with one stone?

It is best to buy two pairs of shoes at the same time. If one shoe is worn out, match it with one from the other pair. If another shoe is worn out, match it with another from the other pair. This is also an excellent economic method.

Warmth in the Heart (167)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 10: Red Flames Fill the Sky, the Courtyard Praises the Filial Daughter; The Red Carpet on the Ground, the Famous Actor is Met on the Spot

They looked at Zuo Shichen and others' tickets. There were three consecutive tickets for the 25th, 26th, and 27th. They happened to be on the left side of the third row. The audience seats in that theater were separated on both sides, with a walkway in the middle covered with a long carpet. At that time, there were already many people who had come to see the play. The place was full of men and women, mostly from academic circles. Because this kind of new play was not something that people in the intellectual class would not want to watch. Even if they watched it, they would not understand it and would not see its good points. Most of the audience who came today were family members and friends of the members of the Qingliu Society. But there were still quite a few people. By 7:15, the place was full. A dark green velvet curtain hung in front of the stage. Below the curtain, there was a row of tassels. Near the tassels, there was a very beautiful lace border. Around the perimeter of the stage, there was a row of electric lights. Outside the electric lights, there was a cover to prevent the light from irritating the eyes of the audience. Before the opening, all the lights in the entire theater were on. When the opening occurred, all the lights in the entire theater were turned off, leaving only the lights on the stage. That could make the scenery exceptionally clear and could make all the eyes of the audience in the entire theater focus on the stage. Therefore, they were paying attention to the lighting. In foreign theaters, there are people who specialize in managing the lighting. Before the opening, someone came out from the curtain to report something to the audience. Do you know who this person was? It was Lu Jun. He talked about the history of how the Qingliu Society was organized, as well as all the polite words asking for guidance. Afterwards, a profit-seeking music team played music, and the opening began immediately. Then, the play was performed act by act. It was strange that when the play was being performed on stage, many audience members did not make any noise. Only the clear words spoken on the stage could be heard. It was only when that act ended that many people started making a lot of noise, discussing the play. In the old theaters, when the actors were singing and speaking on the stage, the audience was noisy and talking about other things. There was no such concentration of attention. After two or three acts, Zuo Shichen asked Ruiyun, "Do you understand the plot of the play?" Ruiyun nodded. She said it was easy to understand because it was all in vernacular. Although they spoke Mandarin,

that kind of Mandarin was also easy to understand. Zuo Shichen smiled and said, "Did you bring several handkerchiefs?" Ruiyun was puzzled and said, "I only have one. Do you need to wipe your hands?" As she spoke, she handed Zuo Shichen a small, pale red silk handkerchief the size of the palm of her hand. Zuo Shichen shook his head and smiled, "It's not that I want to wipe my hands. The next two acts will be very sad. You will definitely cry when you see them. That's why I told you to prepare a handkerchief." Ruiyun said, "You mean I'm going to use it to wipe my tears? No, no. My heart is the hardest. I won't cry even if I encounter something sad. Besides, this is just a play. It's not real."

Yesterday, the fine cloth of this factory's cotton cloth rebounded, with a great tendency to reach the peak. This is because the actual sales are smooth, but the stock bottom is empty. The factory's opening loan has been sold to July, and the goods in May and June have also been sold. And the number of dealers who sell to the customer gang is very large, and they have not yet been delivered. The Tianjin gang has settled the price according to the current market, which makes the market higher and higher. The turnover of dyed cloth is still smooth, so the tight situation is rare in recent years. Fine twill is softer with blue double fish, and Yanghe is also quite clever. Crude cloth Tianjin gang traded more than 200 pieces, but the crude twill turnover is still sluggish.

The market situation of East-West textiles has turned stable, and the rising wind of East goods has subsided. The actual sales are not moving, so there is no ability to continue to rise. Yesterday, fine, Zhigong Ni, etc. were unchanged. Although there is a saying that white crepe cloth has increased in price, but the hand goods are still sold at three taels. The dealer opened at three taels and one qian. Dian Qiuxiang Yuanyang yarn, which was once in short supply, will arrive next Monday, and the opening price is eight taels and four qian half. Tang Taizong is still eight taels and two qian half. Light-colored printed colors are added in this street. Tang Taizong sells one qian nine fen half, Shou Lao riding a deer two qian, Chongsu silk Xuzhou Zhoucun and other gangs slightly added, yesterday cute beauty Zha blue three taels nine qian, foreign blue three taels eight qian, civilization style has arrived in Shanghai in large quantities, the price is from one qian seven fen to one qian seven fen seven li and a half, Western goods bleached cloth Yangtze River Gang is quite active, Heji Guan Bao opened ten taels, Taihe Chicken eleven taels two qian half, all have been sold.

Oil Market: The Rising and Falling of the Asphalt Market

Asphalt sales have been divided equally between candle making and soap making for nearly ten years. At the beginning of this late spring, candle makers are preparing for the summer season, and soap factories are also preparing raw materials because soap sales are about to boom. However, since the two famous soap factories in Shanghai sold soap at a low price two years ago, all smaller soap factories have been affected and have reduced their scope, so sales have also changed accordingly. In the past, retail sales were more common, but now they have become integer. The more small soap factories there are, the more retail sales are booming, and the more large soap factories promote their business, the more integer there are. Although the sales of each asphalt line have not decreased, the conversion from retail to integer is not as profitable as before. Because large soap factories are serious about purchasing goods, the price is also harsh,

unlike small soap factories that can settle for cheaper prices without paying attention to the quality of the goods. As for the candle making end, because the summer season must take high-quality materials, unlike soap making, which only takes cheap prices and does not talk about the quality of the goods. Recently, both kinds of supplies are in demand, and sales are endless. Because the source of Hankou's market was not prosperous half a month ago, the price of the factory's asphalt rose to fourteen taels and eight qian, and then fell to thirteen taels and four qian due to the arrival of goods. Chongjing also rose to fifteen taels. However, the occasional shortage of goods during the spring season will see a rise, only the pyramid flower will appear and cannot last. According to the recent details of the Hankou letter, there are more incoming goods of hemp oil, and the market is also flat. Zhu Hong Chongjing is at fourteen taels, Sanheng is at thirteen taels and enters money, Zazhong and Zhijiang are at thirteen taels six or seven qian, Pingjing is at thirteen taels four or five qian, and Tianjin is at thirteen taels two or three qian. The spring flood in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has not yet started, and the incoming goods cannot rush in for a while, so the market is not too cheap.

Hardware: Military Metal Products Trading Alone is Booming

No. 14, new lead wire, etc., each have one or two thousand dan. In addition, white lead skin, black iron skin, angle iron, tin, and copper are also said to be many.

As for the main road goods such as plain white iron, French West nails, and English steel plates, there have been very few transactions recently, and the market is quite lonely.

Social News

Late Marriage and Celibacy in Ireland

By Fran.

The recently published Volume 5 of the 1926 census of the Irish Free State, a portion of which is specifically devoted to discussing the marriage age and reproductive status of the people of that nation,

is capable of arousing a strong interest in readers. It is claimed that the male and female citizens of the Free State marry particularly late,

and even those who remain unmarried for life are quite numerous. Generally speaking, among men between the ages of twenty-five and thirty, those who are unmarried account for 80 percent; between thirty-five and forty, the unmarried account for 5 percent; and between fifty-five and sixty-five, the unmarried account for 26 percent.

Such figures can truly be considered unique in the world. Among European countries, the closest comparison to Ireland is Sweden, where the percentages of unmarried men in the three age groups mentioned above are 64, 25, and 12. Next are places like Finland, Northern Ireland, and Estonia, which are roughly similar to Sweden. As for Italy, the percentages of unmarried men in these three age groups are 53, 17, and 9 respectively. Scotland and Denmark are similar. England and Wales have figures of 45, 16,

and 10. Portugal and Germany are roughly similar to England.

Regarding women, the Irish Free State also consistently shows that they are among the women who marry the latest or the least. The following is a table listing their ages and the percentage of unmarried women:

Age　Percentage

25 to 30　62

30 to 35　42

35 to 40　32

55 to 65　24

At the same time, in Northern Ireland, unmarried women account for 52 percent of those between 25 and 30 years old, 31 percent of those between 35 and 40 years old, and 26 percent of those between 55 and 60 years old. Sweden, Finland, and Switzerland show similar figures, but the percentage of unmarried women between 55 and 65 years old is all below 20. As for England and Wales, the figures are 41, 20, and 15. The percentages of unmarried women in other countries such as Denmark, Italy, and Germany are lower in every age group.

According to the Director of Statistics of the Free State, the number of people resisting marriage among the residents of the 26 counties has increased year by year since 1841.

In that year, only 43 percent of all men between 25 and 35 years old were unmarried, but by 1926, this had risen to 72 percent. Furthermore, in 1861, unmarried men between 55 and 65 years old

accounted for only 11 percent, but by 1926, this had risen to 26 percent.

The situation for women is generally the same. In 1841, unmarried women accounted for only 28 percent of all women between 25 and 35 years old, but by 1926, this had risen to as high as 53 percent. Furthermore, in 1861, unmarried women accounted for only 13 percent of women between 55 and 65 years old, but by 1926, the number of old maids in this age group had increased to as high as 24 percent.

If one were to say that the desire to emigrate is the reason for the increasing trend of resisting marriage, I am afraid that this reason would not be satisfactory. This is because if one intends to emigrate, one should marry as early as possible. According to the analysis of figures, men in the rural areas of the Free State marry much later than those in the cities, and men in the cities of the Free State marry much later than those in the cities of other countries. However, this is not so true for women. If one were to say that this is due to the oppression of poverty, this would not be an appropriate explanation either, because the average wealth per person in Ireland is indeed greater than in 1880, 1860, and 1840, but the marriage ages of men and women were much earlier at that time. How can this be explained?

However, although men and women in the Free State marry later

and less often, the reproductive capacity of women in that country is indeed not small. Generally speaking, the ratio of children under the age of five to married women under the age of forty-five is as high as 131 percent, which must be said to be the highest ratio in all of Europe, because Norway accounts for 118 percent,

Finland accounts for 114 percent, Sweden accounts for 103 percent,

Canada accounts for 96 percent, Denmark accounts for 93 percent, New Zealand accounts for 82 percent, Germany accounts for 75 percent, and England and Wales account for 71 percent. Ireland has consistently maintained this record since 1861, while only England and Wales have decreased from 116 to 71.

Because women have such a high fertility rate, even if they marry late, the result is that Irish children can still receive a fair distribution, and there is no fear of scarcity. Therefore, among every hundred people aged fifteen to sixty-five in that country,

there are an average of 47 children under the age of fifteen. Compared with other countries, Portugal and Norway both have 53, Italy and Denmark both have 50, England and Wales have 37, Sweden, Finland, and Switzerland all have 43, and France has the fewest, with only 32, while the Free State is unwilling to show weakness in this regard.

The lives of women in the Free State are not as comfortable as those of women in England, and the situation of most unmarried women is particularly difficult, but the lives of their men are better than those of England, and can even be ranked first in the world. This is because the agricultural situation in that country is suitable for men.

China Should Design to Attract Foreign Tourists

The China Review states that Shanghai is a thoroughfare for tourists coming and going in the Far East, but it has not become a tourist center, which is a great pity. According to the statistics of various shipping companies, nearly 40,000 tourists from various countries in the world pass through Shanghai every year, but Shanghai actually lacks scenic spots that can make foreign guests linger and enjoy themselves. From a national and economic point of view, this is all a pity. Since tourists arrive in Shanghai, they have nothing to miss, and at most stay for one or two days before leaving, which causes the local commercial sector to lose a great opportunity. Assuming that 40,000 tourists spend 100 Mexican dollars a day, the Shanghai public can enjoy a profit of 4 million dollars a year. If these 40,000 people can be induced to stay for ten days, a profit of 40 million dollars can be obtained.

Switzerland, France, Germany, Italy, Spain, Japan, and other countries

all attract tourists to reap commercial benefits. This year, Japan is spending 100,000 dollars in advertising expenses in the United States to recruit tourists. Manila is also using various methods to attract tourists, such as carnivals.

Attracting tourists, foreigners coming to the Far East in the future will follow one after another. Shanghai should quickly catch up and create an important tourist destination in the East. The first thing to do is to seek convenience for tourists. Although Shanghai lacks good scenery, it is not far from Suzhou, Hangzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, and Songjiang. Trains can reach these places directly. In addition to West Lake, Hangzhou has extremely good scenic spots in its vicinity. The automobile road is under construction. Now it is appropriate to rush to build the Hangzhou-Shanghai automobile road and build a first-class modern hotel in Hangzhou that can accommodate hundreds of people, with equipment for boating, horse riding, fishing, etc. In addition, automobile roads should also be opened between Shanghai and Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing, with various sports facilities attached.

If a park can be built along the edge of Lake Tai in Wuxi, it will surely be a popular destination for foreigners.

This kind of major project requires an investment of several million dollars, but in the future, it can absorb hundreds of millions of foreign dollars, which is worth spending. When Chinese and foreign tourists are prosperous, local commerce will flourish greatly, and Shanghai residents will also have a place to visit and relax on weekends and holidays. Other provinces have made great progress in opening automobile roads, but Shanghai alone is lagging behind, which is very strange. According to the report of the Road Improvement Association, the mileage of all automobile roads in China has increased from 4,000 miles in the tenth year of the Republic of China to 86,000 miles in the nineteenth year of the Republic of China.

Between the fourteenth and nineteenth years, it doubled. In the single year of the eighteenth year, it increased by 23,000 miles, but Shanghai's automobile roads are still very lacking. This matter should be urgently planned and implemented by a committee jointly formed by the central government and the authorities of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and should not be delayed any longer. After this move is completed, all parties will benefit from it, which is much more glorious for the country than welcoming a foreign prince and embracing Buddha's feet at the last minute, demolishing the thatched huts of the poor on a large scale.

However, it must be noted that the construction of automobile roads must be a truly good road, and should not be like Nanjing's Zhongshan Avenue, which is only in name. It is especially hoped that the cost of road construction will be reduced as much as possible, and should not be like Zhongshan Avenue, which wastes huge amounts of money. As far as we know, some officials in the interior have forcibly occupied people's land and houses and included them in the automobile road route without giving adequate compensation. This is done in the name of national construction, which is very inappropriate. It is deeply hoped that this will not happen again when building roads in the future. We would rather Shanghai lose 40 million dollars a year than see the poor people of China suffer this tyranny. In short, whether the Danish prince and American rich can see China's "paradise on earth" (referring to Suzhou and Hangzhou) has little to do with our people, but that private property of the people should forever be private property of the people

is very important.

Four New Planets Beyond Neptune

Probably No Human Habitation

Rome Dispatch: Professor Bian Tangdi, a famous Italian astronomer and meteorologist, discovered four new planets beyond Neptune. He is now discussing his research with guests, saying that he does not believe that humans live on these new planets. "These planets are extremely far from the sun, and their material conditions are very underdeveloped. Therefore, to say that humans live there is nonsense. These planets are still in an embryonic state and are millions of years behind Earth. Their development will take millions of years more. I used all the mathematical methods used by astronomers to discover these new planets. As such, it proves that the scope of the solar system is much larger than imagined,

in fact, about fifty times larger than currently imagined," he said.

British Farmers Decide to Try Planting Artificial Cotton

Another New Industry

London Dispatch: More than two hundred farmers near Shipley, England, held a meeting and decided to try planting a kind of grass that can replace cotton. In the future, this grass will be used instead of cotton. If it is successful, it will be cheaper than real cotton. It is expected that Shipley will become the center of this new industry.

The Human Body is Worth Only Two and a Half Dollars Chemically

Determined by the British Health Insurance Association

According to the research results of the medical department of the British National Health Insurance Commission, the chemical value of the human body is, on average, only about two and a half Chinese silver dollars per person. The chemical substances in the body are as follows:

Enough fat to make seven bars of soap,

Enough iron to make one medium-sized nail,

Enough lime to fill a small sugar bowl,

Enough lime to whitewash a chicken coop,

Enough phosphorus to make 2,200 matches,

Enough salt to make a pinch of salt,

Enough potassium to explode a toy firecracker,

Enough sulfur to remove fleas from a dog's body.

Publishing News

Mr. Zeng Wanshi announced that the New Culture Daily, which I co-founded with Mr. Hu Ruirong in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, was once popular for a time, with a circulation of more than 10,000 copies. Later, it was suspended for some reason, and readers expressed their regret. However, at that time, there were 200 copies reserved for subscription, which were not issued due to other reasons. Now I have bound the newspapers into volumes, a total of 80 issues, divided into two volumes, upper and lower.

The style is exquisite, and the two volumes are only sold for one big ocean. If you want to buy them, you can send the fee to Fufeng Society, Quanjiatuan Road, Qiju East, to purchase them from me. There are also many other small newspapers, with a catalog printed and sent by mail upon request.

The Wu Ben Shu Pharmacy announced that the Dianxue Fa in Chinese martial arts

was created by Zhang Sanfeng in the Ming Dynasty, who passed it on to Wang Yipiao. It is known as the Wudang School. Wang's disciples flourished in Zhejiang. Those who are proficient in this way can defend themselves and punish evil. Many famous masters and heroes in the early Qing Dynasty were proficient in this way. Amazing anecdotes spread at home and abroad. Mei Zhanchun of Longquan was also a giant of the Wudang orthodox school in the early Qing Dynasty. He was especially proficient in Dianxue healing. His posthumous works were found by modern people and published by Wu Ben Shu Pharmacy. It is named "The Secret of Guoshu Dianxue" and "Combined Edition of Injury Point Treatment Method". The techniques, pointing methods, solutions, and medicinal methods are all wonderful. Each book costs 3.2 cents, and 7 cents will be added for out-of-town shipments. The sales offices are Guomin Bookstore on Qipan Street and Huatong Bookstore on Sima Road, Shanghai.
